TITLE: Kubectl Explain Command Examples
DESCRIPTION: Practical examples demonstrating how to use `kubectl explain` to get documentation for resources, all their fields recursively, specific API versions, and individual fields of a resource.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubectl/generated/kubectl_explain/_index.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Get the documentation of the resource and its fields
kubecl explain pods

# Get all the fields in the resource
kubecl explain pods --recursive

# Get the explanation for deployment in supported api versions
kubecl explain deployments --api-version=apps/v1

# Get the documentation of a specific field of a resource
kubecl explain pods.spec.containers

# Get the documentation of resources in different format
kubecl explain deployment --output=plaintext-openapiv2
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API: Resource Version Parameters for Get, List, and Watch
DESCRIPTION: Describes the `resourceVersion` and `resourceVersionMatch` parameters used in `get`, `list`, and `watch` operations, detailing how the API server interprets them to ensure data consistency and control matching behavior for resource retrieval.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_43

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
API Query Parameters:
  resourceVersion: string
    Operations: get, list, watch
    Description: Specifies the server's internal version of an object for consistency. Must be treated as opaque by clients.
    Behavior: Interpreted differently based on operation and value.
  resourceVersionMatch: string
    Operations: list (from v1.19)
    Description: Affects how matching happens when resourceVersion is set.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Kubernetes Watch: Get State and Start at Any Semantic
DESCRIPTION: Explains the 'Get State and Start at Any' semantic for Kubernetes `watch` operations. The watch can start at any resource version, potentially older, and begins with synthetic 'Added' events for all existing resources at the starting version. Clients should be aware of potential data staleness.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_52

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Start a **watch** at any resource version; the most recent resource version
available is preferred, but not required. Any starting resource version is
allowed. It is possible for the **watch** to start at a much older resource
version that the client has previously observed, particularly in high availability
configurations, due to partitions or stale caches. Clients that cannot tolerate
this apparent rewinding should not start a **watch** with this semantic. To
establish initial state, the **watch** begins with synthetic ""Added"" events for
all resource instances that exist at the starting resource version. All following
watch events are for all changes that occurred after the resource version the
**watch** started at.

**watches** initialized this way may return arbitrarily stale
data. Please review this semantic before using it, and favor the other semantics
where possible.
```

TITLE: kubectl get command examples
DESCRIPTION: A collection of practical examples demonstrating common uses of the `kubectl get` command, including listing pods, specifying output formats, filtering resources, and querying across namespaces.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubectl/generated/kubectl_get/_index.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List all pods in ps output format
kubectl get pods
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List all pods in ps output format with more information (such as node name)
kubectl get pods -o wide
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List a single replication controller with specified NAME in ps output format
kubectl get replicationcontroller web
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List deployments in JSON output format, in the ""v1"" version of the ""apps"" API group
kubectl get deployments.v1.apps -o json
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List a single pod in JSON output format
kubectl get -o json pod web-pod-13je7
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List a pod identified by type and name specified in ""pod.yaml"" in JSON output format
kubectl get -f pod.yaml -o json
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List resources from a directory with kustomization.yaml - e.g. dir/kustomization.yaml
kubectl get -k dir/
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Return only the phase value of the specified pod
kubectl get -o template pod/web-pod-13je7 --template={{.status.phase}}
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List resource information in custom columns
kubectl get pod test-pod -o custom-columns=CONTAINER:.spec.containers[0].name,IMAGE:.spec.containers[0].image
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List all replication controllers and services together in ps output format
kubectl get rc,services
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List one or more resources by their type and names
kubectl get rc/web service/frontend pods/web-pod-13je7
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List the 'status' subresource for a single pod
kubectl get pod web-pod-13je7 --subresource status
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List all deployments in namespace 'backend'
kubectl get deployments.apps --namespace backend
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List all pods existing in all namespaces
kubectl get pods --all-namespaces
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API: Example APIGroupList JSON Response

      ""versions"": [
        {
          ""groupVersion"": ""apiregistration.k8s.io/v1"",
          ""version"": ""v1""
        }
      ],
      ""preferredVersion"": {
        ""groupVersion"": ""apiregistration.k8s.io/v1"",
        ""version"": ""v1""
      }

      ""name"": ""apps"",
      ""versions"": [
        {
          ""groupVersion"": ""apps/v1"",
          ""version"": ""v1""
        }
      ],
      ""preferredVersion"": {
        ""groupVersion"": ""apps/v1"",
        ""version"": ""v1""
      }
    },
    ...
}
```

TITLE: Content Best Practice: Use Simple and Direct Language

:--| :-----

```

TITLE: Mermaid Flowchart of Documentation Topics
DESCRIPTION: This Mermaid flowchart illustrates the structure and key topics covered in the documentation section. It outlines the relationship between Mermaid.js, diagram creation methods, examples, styling, and tips, starting from the utility of diagrams.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/contribute/style/diagram-guide.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: Mermaid
CODE:
```
flowchart LR
    subgraph m[Mermaid.js]
    direction TB
        S[ ]-.-
        C[build<br>diagrams<br>with markdown] -->
        D[on-line<br>live editor]
    end
    A[Why are diagrams<br>useful?] --> m
    m --> N[3 x methods<br>for creating<br>diagrams]
    N --> T[Examples]
    T --> X[Styling<br>and<br>captions]
    X --> V[Tips]
    
 
    classDef box fill:#fff,stroke:#000,stroke-width:1px,color:#000;
    classDef spacewhite fill:#ffffff,stroke:#fff,stroke-width:0px,color:#000
    class A,C,D,N,X,m,T,V box
    class S spacewhite
```

TITLE: Suggestions for More In-depth Kubernetes Documentation Content
DESCRIPTION: Respondents requested more advanced configuration examples, in-depth use cases, and production-like examples, along with a clearer 'Quick Start' guide to address information overload for experienced users.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2019-10-29-2019-sig-docs-survey.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: text
CODE:
```
-  ...But since we're talking about docs, more is always better. More
advanced configuration examples would be, to me, the way to go. Like a Use Case page for each
configuration topic with beginner to advanced example scenarios. Something like that would be
awesome....
- More in-depth examples and use cases would be great. I often feel that the Kubernetes
documentation scratches the surface of a topic, which might be great for new users, but it leaves
more experienced users without much ""official"" guidance on how to implement certain things.
- More production like examples in the resource sections (notably secrets) or links to production like
examples
- It would be great to see a very clear ""Quick Start"" A->Z up and running like many other tech
projects. There are a handful of almost-quick-starts, but no single guidance. The result is
information overkill.
```

TITLE: Kubernetes Watch: Get State and Start at Most Recent Semantic
DESCRIPTION: Describes the 'Get State and Start at Most Recent' semantic for Kubernetes `watch` operations. The watch starts at the most recent, consistent resource version (from etcd via quorum read) and generates synthetic 'Added' events for initial state.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_53

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Start a **watch** at the most recent resource version, which must be consistent
(in detail: served from etcd via a quorum read). To establish initial state,
the **watch** begins with synthetic ""Added"" events of all resources instances
that exist at the starting resource version. All following watch events are for
all changes that occurred after the resource version the **watch** started at.
```

|-----------------------|---------------------|----------------------------------------|
| Most Recent           | Any                 | Not older than                         |
```

TITLE: Go Example for RawExtension and JSON Serialization
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates the usage of `runtime.RawExtension` in Go for handling arbitrary data in Kubernetes API objects, showing how internal and external Go structs are defined and how they translate to JSON on the wire.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/extend-resources/device-class-v1beta2.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: Go
CODE:
```
// Internal package:

	type MyAPIObject struct {
		runtime.TypeMeta `json:"",inline""`
		MyPlugin runtime.Object `json:""myPlugin""`
	}

	type PluginA struct {
		AOption string `json:""aOption""`
	}

// External package:

	type MyAPIObject struct {
		runtime.TypeMeta `json:"",inline""`
		MyPlugin runtime.RawExtension `json:""myPlugin""`
	}

	type PluginA struct {
		AOption string `json:""aOption""`
	}

// On the wire, the JSON will look something like this:

	{
		""kind"":""MyAPIObject"",
		""apiVersion"":""v1"",
		""myPlugin"": {
			""kind"":""PluginA"",
			""aOption"":""foo"",
		},
	}
```

TITLE: Example VolumeSnapshotClass Definitions
DESCRIPTION: Provides examples of `VolumeSnapshotClass` YAML definitions. The first example shows a default snapshot class using an annotation, while the second includes additional parameters and secret references for a CSI driver, demonstrating how to configure snapshot creation behavior.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2018-10-09-volume-snapshot-alpha.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
apiVersion: snapshot.storage.k8s.io/v1alpha1
kind: VolumeSnapshotClass
metadata:
  name: default-snapclass
  annotations:
    snapshot.storage.kubernetes.io/is-default-class: ""true""
snapshotter: com.example.csi-driver


apiVersion: snapshot.storage.k8s.io/v1alpha1
kind: VolumeSnapshotClass
metadata:
  name: csi-snapclass
snapshotter: com.example.csi-driver
parameters:
  fakeSnapshotOption: foo
  csiSnapshotterSecretName: csi-secret
  csiSnapshotterSecretNamespace: csi-namespace
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API: Verifying Response Compression
DESCRIPTION: This example shows how to verify if API response compression is active. By including an `Accept-Encoding: gzip` header in a GET or LIST request, the client can request a compressed response. The presence of a `content-encoding: gzip` header in the server's response confirms that the content was compressed.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_16

LANGUAGE: http
CODE:
```
GET /api/v1/pods
Accept-Encoding: gzip
---
200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
content-encoding: gzip
...
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API Paths for Collections and Specific Resources
DESCRIPTION: Details the HTTP GET paths for retrieving collections of resources and individual resources, distinguishing between cluster-scoped and namespace-scoped resources.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Cluster-scoped resources:
  GET /apis/GROUP/VERSION/RESOURCETYPE
  GET /apis/GROUP/VERSION/RESOURCETYPE/NAME

Namespace-scoped resources:
  GET /apis/GROUP/VERSION/RESOURCETYPE
  GET /apis/GROUP/VERSION/namespaces/NAMESPACE/RESOURCETYPE
  GET /apis/GROUP/VERSION/namespaces/NAMESPACE/RESOURCETYPE/NAME

Namespace collection/detail:
  GET /api/v1/namespaces
  GET /api/v1/namespaces/NAME
```

TITLE: Example Kubernetes AuthenticationConfiguration File Structure

#          Do not use this for your own cluster!
#
apiVersion: apiserver.config.k8s.io/v1beta1
kind: AuthenticationConfiguration
# list of authenticators to authenticate Kubernetes users using JWT compliant tokens.
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API: List Request resourceVersion and resourceVersionMatch Combinations
DESCRIPTION: Details the behavior of Kubernetes `list` requests based on various combinations of `resourceVersion`, `resourceVersionMatch`, and paging parameters like `limit` and `continue`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_46

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
| resourceVersionMatch param          | paging params                  | resourceVersion not set | resourceVersion=""0"" | resourceVersion=""{value other than 0}"" |
|-------------------------------------|--------------------------------|-------------------------|---------------------|----------------------------------------|
| _unset_                             | _limit unset_                  | Most Recent             | Any                 | Not older than                         |
| _unset_                             | limit=\<n\>, _continue unset_  | Most Recent             | Any                 | Exact                                  |
| _unset_                             | limit=\<n\>, continue=\<token\>| Continuation            | Continuation        | Invalid, HTTP `400 Bad Request`        |
| `resourceVersionMatch=Exact`        | _limit unset_                  | Invalid                 | Invalid             | Exact                                  |
| `resourceVersionMatch=Exact`        | limit=\<n\>, _continue unset_  | Invalid                 | Invalid             | Exact                                  |
| `resourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan` | _limit unset_                  | Invalid                 | Any                 | Not older than                         |
| `resourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan` | limit=\<n\>, _continue unset_  | Invalid                 | Any                 | Not older than                         |
```

TITLE: PodDisruptionBudget API Migration to policy/v1
DESCRIPTION: Covers the deprecation of the policy/v1beta1 API version for PodDisruptionBudget as of Kubernetes v1.25. It guides users to migrate to the policy/v1 API, specifically detailing the changed behavior of an empty 'spec.selector' field.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
PodDisruptionBudget API Migration:
  Deprecated: policy/v1beta1 (removed in v1.25)
  Migrate to: policy/v1 (available since v1.21)

  Notable changes in policy/v1:
    - spec.selector:
      - An empty {} selector in policy/v1 selects all pods in the namespace.
      - In policy/v1beta1, an empty {} selector selected no pods.
      - An unset spec.selector selects no pods in either API version.
```

TITLE: Migrate CertificateSigningRequest to v1 API
DESCRIPTION: The certificates.k8s.io/v1beta1 API version of CertificateSigningRequest is no longer served as of v1.22. Migrate manifests and API clients to use the certificates.k8s.io/v1 API version, available since v1.19. All existing persisted objects are accessible via the new API.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_17

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Resource: CertificateSigningRequest
Old API Version: certificates.k8s.io/v1beta1 (deprecated in v1.22)
New API Version: certificates.k8s.io/v1 (available since v1.19)

Notable Changes in certificates.k8s.io/v1:
For API clients requesting certificates:
- spec.signerName: Now required; requests for kubernetes.io/legacy-unknown are not allowed.
- spec.usages: Now required, may not contain duplicate values, and must only contain known usages.
For API clients approving or signing certificates:
- status.conditions: May not contain duplicate types.
- status.conditions[*].status: Now required.
- status.certificate: Must be PEM-encoded and contain only CERTIFICATE blocks.
```

TITLE: Haskell Client Example: Listing Pods with Kubeconfig
DESCRIPTION: This Haskell code snippet demonstrates how to initialize the Kubernetes client using a kubeconfig file. It shows the setup of the client configuration and then dispatches a request to list all pods across all namespaces, printing the JSON response. The example highlights the use of `mkKubeClientConfig` and `dispatchMime` for API interaction.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/tasks/administer-cluster/access-cluster-api.md#_snippet_19

LANGUAGE: haskell
CODE:
```
exampleWithKubeConfig :: IO ()
exampleWithKubeConfig = do
    oidcCache <- atomically $ newTVar $ Map.fromList []
    (mgr, kcfg) <- mkKubeClientConfig oidcCache $ KubeConfigFile ""/path/to/kubeconfig""
    dispatchMime
            mgr
            kcfg
            (CoreV1.listPodForAllNamespaces (Accept MimeJSON))
        >>= print
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API Resource Versioning Concepts
DESCRIPTION: Details on how resource versions are handled in Kubernetes API requests, focusing on 'Exact' and 'Continuation' behaviors, and the impact of caching and client-side considerations.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_50

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Resource Versioning Concepts:

Exact:
  - Description: Returns data at the exact resource version provided. If unavailable, server responds with HTTP 410 Gone.
  - List Requests with resourceVersionMatch: Guarantees collection's .metadata.resourceVersion matches requested version (does not apply to individual items).
  - Serving Source:
    - Default: Served from _etcd_.
    - With ListFromCacheSnapshot feature gate: Attempts to serve from snapshot if available (improves performance, reduces etcd load).
    - Cache Snapshot Duration: Kept for 75 seconds; fallback to etcd if resourceVersion unavailable.

Continuation:
  - Description: Returns the next page of data for a paginated list request, ensuring consistency with the initial request's resourceVersion.
  - Continue Token: Response to list requests with limit includes a _continue token_ encoding resourceVersion and last observed position.
  - If resourceVersion in continue token unavailable: Server responds with HTTP 410 Gone.
  - Serving Source:
    - Default: Served from _etcd_.
    - With ListFromCacheSnapshot feature gate: Attempts to serve from snapshot if available (improves performance, reduces etcd load).
    - Cache Snapshot Duration: Kept for 75 seconds; fallback to etcd if resourceVersion in continue token unavailable.

Important Note on List Metadata:
  - When listing resources, response includes list metadata of the collection and object metadata for each item.
  - For individual objects within a collection response, .metadata.resourceVersion tracks when that object was last updated, not its up-to-dateness when served.

Client Handling Considerations:
  - When using resourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan and limit is set: Clients must handle HTTP 410 Gone responses (e.g., retry with a newer resourceVersion or fall back to resourceVersion="""").
  - When using resourceVersionMatch=Exact and limit is unset: Clients must verify that the collection's .metadata.resourceVersion matches the requested resourceVersion, and handle mismatches (e.g., fall back to a request with limit set).
```

TITLE: Migrate CustomResourceDefinition to v1 API
DESCRIPTION: The apiextensions.k8s.io/v1beta1 API version of CustomResourceDefinition is no longer served as of v1.22. Migrate manifests and API clients to use the apiextensions.k8s.io/v1 API version, available since v1.16. All existing persisted objects are accessible via the new API.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_13

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Resource: CustomResourceDefinition
Old API Version: apiextensions.k8s.io/v1beta1 (deprecated in v1.22)
New API Version: apiextensions.k8s.io/v1 (available since v1.16)

Notable Changes:
- spec.scope: No longer defaulted to Namespaced; must be explicitly specified.
- spec.version: Removed in v1; use spec.versions instead.
- spec.validation: Removed in v1; use spec.versions[*].schema instead.
- spec.subresources: Removed in v1; use spec.versions[*].subresources instead.
- spec.additionalPrinterColumns: Removed in v1; use spec.versions[*].additionalPrinterColumns instead.
- spec.conversion.webhookClientConfig: Moved to spec.conversion.webhook.clientConfig in v1.
- spec.conversion.conversionReviewVersions: Moved to spec.conversion.webhook.conversionReviewVersions in v1.
- spec.versions[*].schema.openAPIV3Schema: Now required when creating v1 CustomResourceDefinition objects; must be a structural schema.
- spec.preserveUnknownFields: true: Disallowed when creating v1 CustomResourceDefinition objects; must be specified within schema definitions as x-kubernetes-preserve-unknown-fields: true.
- additionalPrinterColumns items: JSONPath field renamed to jsonPath in v1.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Kubernetes API: Handling Unavailable Resource Versions (List/Get/Watch)
DESCRIPTION: Describes how Kubernetes API servers respond to `list`, `get`, or `watch` requests with unrecognized or unavailable `resourceVersion` values. For `list`/`get`, it may result in `504 (Gateway Timeout)` or a `Retry-After` header. For `watch`, the server may wait indefinitely.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_56

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Servers are not required to serve unrecognized resource versions. If you request
**list** or **get** for a resource version that the API server does not recognize,
then the API server may either:

* wait briefly for the resource version to become available, then timeout with a
  `504 (Gateway Timeout)` if the provided resource versions does not become available
  in a reasonable amount of time;
* respond with a `Retry-After` response header indicating how many seconds a client
  should wait before retrying the request.

If you request a resource version that an API server does not recognize, the
kube-apiserver additionally identifies its error responses with a message
`Too large resource version`.

If you make a **watch** request for an unrecognized resource version, the API server
may wait indefinitely (until the request timeout) for the resource version to become
available.
```

TITLE: Swagger-codegen Generated Documentation for Read Pod API
DESCRIPTION: This snippet illustrates how Swagger-codegen can generate human-readable API documentation from an OpenAPI specification. It details the `GET` endpoint for reading Pods, including path parameters (`name`, `namespace`), consumed media types, and query parameters (`pretty`, `exact`, `export`), providing a clear overview of the API's usage.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2016-12-00-Kubernetes-Supports-Openapi.md#_snippet_2

GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/pods/{name}

(readCoreV1NamespacedPod)

read the specified Pod

Path parameters

name (required)

Path Parameter — name of the Pod

namespace (required)

Path Parameter — object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects

Consumes

This API call consumes the following media types via the Content-Type request header:

-
*/*


Query parameters

pretty (optional)

Query Parameter — If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.

exact (optional)

Query Parameter — Should the export be exact. Exact export maintains cluster-specific fields like 'Namespace'.

export (optional)

Query Parameter — Should this value be exported. Export strips fields that a user can not specify.
```

TITLE: Event API Migration to events.k8s.io/v1
DESCRIPTION: Details the deprecation of the events.k8s.io/v1beta1 API version for Event resources as of Kubernetes v1.25. It provides instructions to migrate manifests and API clients to the events.k8s.io/v1 API, highlighting key changes in field names, types, and new required fields.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Event API Migration:
  Deprecated: events.k8s.io/v1beta1 (removed in v1.25)
  Migrate to: events.k8s.io/v1 (available since v1.19)

  Notable changes in events.k8s.io/v1:
    - type: limited to 'Normal' and 'Warning'
    - involvedObject: renamed to 'regarding'
    - action: required when creating new Events
    - reason: required when creating new Events
    - reportingController: required when creating new Events
    - reportingInstance: required when creating new Events
    - eventTime: use instead of deprecated firstTimestamp
    - series.lastObservedTime: use instead of deprecated lastTimestamp
    - series.count: use instead of deprecated count
    - reportingController: use instead of deprecated source.component
    - reportingInstance: use instead of deprecated source.host
```

TITLE: Kubernetes SubjectAccessReview Request Example
DESCRIPTION: This JSON snippet demonstrates a SubjectAccessReview request, which is used to programmatically check if a user (or subject) has permission to perform a specific action on a resource in Kubernetes. In this example, it checks if a user can 'get' (read) 'pods' in the 'projectCaribou' namespace, belonging to the 'unicorn.example.org' group. This request is sent to the Kubernetes API server for authorization evaluation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/concepts/security/controlling-access.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: json
CODE:
```
{
  ""apiVersion"": ""authorization.k8s.io/v1beta1"",
  ""kind"": ""SubjectAccessReview"",
  ""spec"": {
    ""resourceAttributes"": {
      ""namespace"": ""projectCaribou"",
      ""verb"": ""get"",
      ""group"": ""unicorn.example.org"",
      ""resource"": ""pods""
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API Group Structure and Naming
DESCRIPTION: Details the structure of Kubernetes API groups, differentiating between the core (legacy) group and named groups, including their respective REST paths and `apiVersion` field conventions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/_index.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
API Groups:
  - Core (Legacy) Group:
      REST Path: /api/v1
      apiVersion: v1 (implicitly, not explicitly in field)
  - Named Groups:
      REST Path: /apis/$GROUP_NAME/$VERSION
      apiVersion: $GROUP_NAME/$VERSION (e.g., batch/v1)
```

TITLE: Create an APIService
DESCRIPTION: Creates a new APIService resource. The request body must contain the full definition of the APIService to be created.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/cluster-resources/api-service-v1.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
HTTP Request:
  POST /apis/apiregistration.k8s.io/v1/apiservices

Parameters:
  - body: APIService, required
    Description: The APIService object to create.
  - dryRun (in query): string
    Description: When present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted.
  - fieldManager (in query): string
    Description: fieldManager is a name associated with the actor or entity that is making these changes.
  - fieldValidation (in query): string
    Description: fieldValidation specifies the server-side validation mode used in the request.
  - pretty (in query): string
    Description: If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.

Response:
  - 200 (APIService): OK
  - 201 (APIService): Created
  - 202 (APIService): Accepted
  - 401: Unauthorized
```

- kubeadm v1.15.x+: Migrate from v1beta1 to v1beta2.
- kubeadm v1.22.x+: Migrate from v1beta2 to v1beta3 (v1beta1 and older no longer supported).
- kubeadm v1.27.x+: v1beta2 and older APIs no longer supported.
- kubeadm v1.31.x+: Migrate from v1beta3 to v1beta4.

TITLE: Kubernetes RoleBinding API Operations

        in: path

      pretty:
        type: string
        in: query
        description: pretty

      ""200"":
        type: RoleBinding
        description: OK
      ""401"":
        description: Unauthorized
  list:
    description: list or watch objects of kind RoleBinding
    httpRequest: GET /apis/rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/rolebindings

TITLE: Kubernetes RESTful API Concepts and Terminology
DESCRIPTION: This section details the fundamental concepts of the Kubernetes API, including its RESTful interface, supported HTTP verbs, specific API terminology like resource types, kinds, collections, resources, sub-resources, object naming rules, and Kubernetes-specific API verbs.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Kubernetes API:
  Interface: Resource-based (RESTful) programmatic interface via HTTP
  Supported HTTP Verbs:
    - GET: Retrieve a single resource (Kubernetes 'get') or a collection (Kubernetes 'list')
    - POST: Create primary resources
    - PUT: Create or update resources (Kubernetes 'create' or 'update')
    - PATCH: Apply partial modifications to resources (Kubernetes 'patch')
    - DELETE: Delete primary resources

  Core Terminology:
    - Resource Type: Name used in the URL (e.g., `pods`, `namespaces`, `services`)
    - Kind: Concrete representation or object schema of a resource type
    - Collection: A list of instances of a resource type
    - Resource (Object): A single instance of a resource type
    - Sub-resources: URI paths below a resource, allowing fine-grained authorization or specific operations (e.g., `eviction` for Pods)

  Object Naming:
    - All creatable objects have a unique `name` for idempotent creation and retrieval.
    - Within a `namespace`, only one object of a given kind can have a given name at a time.
    - Non-namespaced objects (e.g., Nodes) must have names unique across the whole cluster.

  Kubernetes API Verbs (distinguished from HTTP verbs):
    - list: Action of returning a collection of resources (HTTP GET without `?watch`)
    - get: Action of retrieving a single resource (HTTP GET)
    - watch: Action of receiving efficient change notifications on resources (HTTP GET with `?watch` query parameter)
    - create: Internal classification for PUT requests when the object does not exist
    - update: Internal classification for PUT requests when the object already exists
    - patch: Corresponds to the HTTP PATCH verb
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API: Requesting Initial State with Watch
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates how to request the initial state of a resource collection as part of a watch request using `sendInitialEvents=true` and `resourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan`. The API server responds with synthetic `ADDED` events for existing objects, followed by a `BOOKMARK` event indicating the synced resource version, and then continues with the regular watch stream.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_15

LANGUAGE: http
CODE:
```
GET /api/v1/namespaces/test/pods?watch=1&sendInitialEvents=true&allowWatchBookmarks=true&resourceVersion=&resourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan
---
200 OK
Transfer-Encoding: chunked
Content-Type: application/json

{
  ""type"": ""ADDED"",
  ""object"": {""kind"": ""Pod"", ""apiVersion"": ""v1"", ""metadata"": {""resourceVersion"": ""8467"", ""name"": ""foo""}, ...}
}
{
  ""type"": ""ADDED"",
  ""object"": {""kind"": ""Pod"", ""apiVersion"": ""v1"", ""metadata"": {""resourceVersion"": ""5726"", ""name"": ""bar""}, ...}
}
{
  ""type"": ""BOOKMARK"",
  ""object"": {""kind"": ""Pod"", ""apiVersion"": ""v1"", ""metadata"": {""resourceVersion"": ""10245""} }
}
...
<followed by regular watch stream starting from resourceVersion=""10245"">
```

TITLE: Migrate SubjectAccessReview Resources to v1 API
DESCRIPTION: The authorization.k8s.io/v1beta1 API version of LocalSubjectAccessReview, SelfSubjectAccessReview, SubjectAccessReview, and SelfSubjectRulesReview is no longer served as of v1.22. Migrate manifests and API clients to use the authorization.k8s.io/v1 API version, available since v1.6.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_16

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Resource: LocalSubjectAccessReview, SelfSubjectAccessReview, SubjectAccessReview, SelfSubjectRulesReview
Old API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1beta1 (deprecated in v1.22)
New API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1 (available since v1.6)

Notable Changes:
- spec.group: Renamed to spec.groups in v1.
```

TITLE: EncryptionConfiguration API Structure and Example (v1)
DESCRIPTION: Defines the complete configuration for encryption providers in the Kubernetes API server. It supports wildcards for specifying resources to encrypt and processes resource lists in order, with earlier lists taking precedence. An example YAML demonstrates how to configure encryption for various resources.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/config-api/apiserver-config.v1.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
EncryptionConfiguration:
  apiVersion: string (apiserver.config.k8s.io/v1)
  kind: string (EncryptionConfiguration)
  properties:
    resources:
      type: []ResourceConfiguration
      required: true
      description: A list containing resources, and their corresponding encryption providers.
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
kind: EncryptionConfiguration
apiVersion: apiserver.config.k8s.io/v1
resources:
- resources:
  - events
  providers:
  - identity: {}  # do not encrypt events even though *.* is specified below
- resources:
  - secrets
  - configmaps
  - pandas.awesome.bears.example
  providers:
  - aescbc:
      keys:
      - name: key1
        secret: c2VjcmV0IGlzIHNlY3VyZQ==
- resources:
  - '*.apps'
  providers:
  - aescbc:
      keys:
      - name: key2
        secret: c2VjcmV0IGlzIHNlY3VyZSwgb3IgaXQ/Cg==
- resources:
  - '*.*'
  providers:
  - aescbc:
      keys:
      - name: key3
        secret: c2VjcmV0IGlzIHNlY3VyZSwgSSB0aGluaw==
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API Versioning Levels and Stability Guidelines
DESCRIPTION: Details the different stability levels for Kubernetes API versions (Alpha, Beta, Stable), including their naming conventions, default enablement status, support guarantees, potential for incompatible changes, and recommended use cases.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/_index.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
API Versioning Levels:
  - Alpha:
    - Version names: contain 'alpha' (e.g., 'v1alpha1').
    - Enablement: Built-in alpha API versions are disabled by default and must be explicitly enabled in the 'kube-apiserver' configuration to be used.
    - Stability: The software may contain bugs. Enabling a feature may expose bugs.
    - Support: Support for an alpha API may be dropped at any time without notice.
    - Compatibility: The API may change in incompatible ways in a later software release without notice.
    - Recommendation: Recommended for use only in short-lived testing clusters, due to increased risk of bugs and lack of long-term support.
  - Beta:
    - Version names: contain 'beta' (e.g., 'v2beta3').
    - Enablement: Built-in beta API versions are disabled by default and must be explicitly enabled in the 'kube-apiserver' configuration to be used (except for beta versions of APIs introduced prior to Kubernetes 1.22, which were enabled by default).
    - Lifetime: Built-in beta API versions have a maximum lifetime of 9 months or 3 minor releases (whichever is longer) from introduction to deprecation, and 9 months or 3 minor releases (whichever is longer) from deprecation to removal.
    - Stability: The software is well tested. Enabling a feature is considered safe.
    - Support: The support for a feature will not be dropped, though the details may change.
    - Compatibility: The schema and/or semantics of objects may change in incompatible ways in a subsequent beta or stable API version. When this happens, migration instructions are provided. Adapting to a subsequent beta or stable API version may require editing or re-creating API objects, and may not be straightforward. The migration may require downtime for applications that rely on the feature.
    - Recommendation: The software is not recommended for production uses. Subsequent releases may introduce incompatible changes. Use of beta API versions is required to transition to subsequent beta or stable API versions once the beta API version is deprecated and no longer served.
  - Stable:
    - Version names: 'vX' where 'X' is an integer.
    - Availability: Stable API versions remain available for all future releases within a Kubernetes major version.
    - Future Plans: There are no current plans for a major version revision of Kubernetes that removes stable APIs.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Migrate Ingress to networking.k8s.io/v1 API
DESCRIPTION: The extensions/v1beta1 and networking.k8s.io/v1beta1 API versions of Ingress are no longer served as of v1.22. Migrate manifests and API clients to use the networking.k8s.io/v1 API version, available since v1.19. All existing persisted objects are accessible via the new API.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_19

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Resource: Ingress
Old API Version: extensions/v1beta1, networking.k8s.io/v1beta1 (deprecated in v1.22)
New API Version: networking.k8s.io/v1 (available since v1.19)

Notable Changes:
- spec.backend: Renamed to spec.defaultBackend.
- serviceName: Renamed to service.name.
- Numeric servicePort: Renamed to service.port.number.
- String servicePort: Renamed to service.port.name.
- pathType: Now required for each specified path. Options are Prefix, Exact, and ImplementationSpecific. Use ImplementationSpecific to match undefined v1beta1 behavior.
```

TITLE: Go Client Example for Pod Resources API
DESCRIPTION: This Go code snippet demonstrates how to establish a gRPC connection to the Pod Resources API via a Unix socket (`/var/lib/kubelet/pod-resources/kubelet.sock`). It then initializes a client and calls the `List` method to retrieve and print the current pod resources, handling potential connection and API call errors.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2020-12-16-third-party-device-metrics-hits-ga.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: go
CODE:
```
func main() {
	ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), connectionTimeout)
	defer cancel()

	socket := ""/var/lib/kubelet/pod-resources/kubelet.sock""
	conn, err := grpc.DialContext(ctx, socket, grpc.WithInsecure(), grpc.WithBlock(),
		grpc.WithDialer(func(addr string, timeout time.Duration) (net.Conn, error) {
			return net.DialTimeout(""unix"", addr, timeout)
		}),
	)

	if err != nil {
		panic(err)
	}

    client := podresourcesapi.NewPodResourcesListerClient(conn)
    resp, err := client.List(ctx, &podresourcesapi.ListPodResourcesRequest{})
	if err != nil {
		panic(err)
	}
	net.Printf(""%+v\n"", resp)
}
```

TITLE: Migrate ReplicaSet API to apps/v1
DESCRIPTION: The extensions/v1beta1, apps/v1beta1, and apps/v1beta2 API versions of ReplicaSet were removed in Kubernetes v1.16. Users should migrate to the apps/v1 API version, available since v1.9. A key change is that `spec.selector` is now required and immutable after creation.

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```

New API: apps/v1 (Available since v1.9)
Migration Notes:
  - `spec.selector` is now required and immutable after creation; use existing template labels as selector for seamless upgrades
```

TITLE: Kubernetes VolumeSnapshotContent Object Definition and Example
DESCRIPTION: Documentation and example YAML for creating a Kubernetes VolumeSnapshotContent object to expose an existing volume snapshot. This object is a non-namespace API object and is typically created by a cluster administrator. It specifies the underlying snapshot details and a reference to the VolumeSnapshot object it should bind to.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2019-12-09-volume-snapshot-beta.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
VolumeSnapshotContent Object Fields:
- driver: CSI driver used to handle this volume. (Required)
- source: Snapshot identifying information
- snapshotHandle: name/identifier of the snapshot. (Required)
- volumeSnapshotRef: Pointer to the VolumeSnapshot object this content should bind to.
- name: Name of the VolumeSnapshot object which the content is bound to.
- namespace: Namespace of the VolumeSnapshot object which the content is bound to.
- deletionPolicy: Valid values are 'Delete' and 'Retain'. If 'Delete', underlying storage snapshot is deleted with VolumeSnapshotContent. If 'Retain', both remain.
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: snapshot.storage.k8s.io/v1beta1
kind: VolumeSnapshotContent
metadata:
  name: manually-created-snapshot-content
spec:
  deletionPolicy: Delete
  driver: testdriver.csi.k8s.io
  source:
    snapshotHandle: 7bdd0de3-aaeb-11e8-9aae-0242ac110002
  volumeSnapshotRef:
    name: test-snapshot
    namespace: default
```

TITLE: Migrate StatefulSet API to apps/v1
DESCRIPTION: The apps/v1beta1 and apps/v1beta2 API versions of StatefulSet were removed in Kubernetes v1.16. Users should migrate to the apps/v1 API version, available since v1.9. Notable changes include `spec.selector` becoming required and immutable, and `spec.updateStrategy.type` now defaulting to `RollingUpdate`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_27

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Resource: StatefulSet
Deprecated API: apps/v1beta1, apps/v1beta2 (Removed in v1.16)
New API: apps/v1 (Available since v1.9)
Migration Notes:
  - `spec.selector` is now required and immutable after creation; use existing template labels as selector for seamless upgrades
  - `spec.updateStrategy.type` now defaults to `RollingUpdate` (was `OnDelete` in `apps/v1beta1`)
```

TITLE: Kubernetes ListMeta API Reference
DESCRIPTION: Detailed API reference for the `ListMeta` object in Kubernetes, including its purpose and the description of its fields.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/common-definitions/list-meta.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
import ""k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1""

ListMeta describes metadata that synthetic resources must have, including lists and various status objects. A resource may have only one of {ObjectMeta, ListMeta}.

Fields:
- continue (string)
  Description: continue may be set if the user set a limit on the number of items returned, and indicates that the server has more data available. The value is opaque and may be used to issue another request to the endpoint that served this list to retrieve the next set of available objects. Continuing a consistent list may not be possible if the server configuration has changed or more than a few minutes have passed. The resourceVersion field returned when using this continue value will be identical to the value in the first response, unless you have received this token from an error message.
- remainingItemCount (int64)
  Description: remainingItemCount is the number of subsequent items in the list which are not included in this list response. If the list request contained label or field selectors, then the number of remaining items is unknown and the field will be left unset and omitted during serialization. If the list is complete (either because it is not chunking or because this is the last chunk), then there are no more remaining items and this field will be left unset and omitted during serialization. Servers older than v1.15 do not set this field. The intended use of the remainingItemCount is *estimating* the size of a collection. Clients should not rely on the remainingItemCount to be set or to be exact.
- resourceVersion (string)
  Description: String that identifies the server's internal version of this object that can be used by clients to determine when objects have changed. Value must be treated as opaque by clients and passed unmodified back to the server. Populated by the system. Read-only. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#concurrency-control-and-consistency
- selfLink (string)
  Description: Deprecated: selfLink is a legacy read-only field that is no longer populated by the system.
```

TITLE: Kubernetes Recommended Labels API Reference
DESCRIPTION: Reference for the standard `app.kubernetes.io` labels, detailing their purpose, type, and examples. These labels are crucial for consistent application metadata across Kubernetes resources, supporting tooling and query capabilities.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/concepts/overview/working-with-objects/common-labels.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
app.kubernetes.io/name: The name of the application (string, e.g., mysql)
app.kubernetes.io/instance: A unique name identifying the instance of an application (string, e.g., mysql-abcxyz)
app.kubernetes.io/version: The current version of the application (string, e.g., 5.7.21, SemVer 1.0, revision hash)
app.kubernetes.io/component: The component within the architecture (string, e.g., database)
app.kubernetes.io/part-of: The name of a higher level application this one is part of (string, e.g., wordpress)
app.kubernetes.io/managed-by: The tool being used to manage the operation of an application (string, e.g., Helm)
```

TITLE: Kubernetes Tutorial Page Content Structure and Guidelines
DESCRIPTION: Defines the required sections and content guidelines for creating a tutorial page in Kubernetes documentation, including section ordering, heading levels, and content types for each part.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/contribute/style/page-content-types.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Tutorial Page Structure:
  - File Location: /content/en/docs/tutorials/
  - Characteristics: Markdown file
  - Required Sections (as comments or shortcodes):
    - overview:
      - Purpose: Set context for the entire topic.
      - Content: Paragraph.
    - prerequisites:
      - Purpose: List necessary conditions/setup.
      - Content: Bullet lists, add additional prerequisites below defaults.
      - Implementation: Use `heading` shortcode.
    - objectives:
      - Purpose: List goals of the tutorial.
      - Content: Bullet lists.
    - lessoncontent:
      - Purpose: Main tutorial steps and narrative.
      - Content: Mix of numbered lists and narrative.
    - cleanup:
      - Purpose: Describe steps to clean up cluster state.
      - Content: Numbered lists.
      - Implementation: Use `heading` shortcode.
    - whatsnext:
      - Purpose: Suggest up to 5 related topics for further reading.
      - Content: Bullet list.
      - Implementation: Use `heading` shortcode.
  - General Guidelines:
    - Use minimum H2 headings (##).
    - Sections are automatically titled by template.
```

TITLE: Kubernetes Resource API v1alpha1 Types Overview
DESCRIPTION: Overview of the new types introduced in the `resource.k8s.io/v1alpha1` API group, detailing their purpose and usage in Kubernetes resource management.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2022-12-15-dynamic-resource-allocation-alpha/index.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
resource.k8s.io/v1alpha1 API Group:
  ResourceClass:
    Description: Defines which resource driver handles a certain kind of resource and provides common parameters for it. Created by a cluster administrator when installing a resource driver.
  ResourceClaim:
    Description: Defines a particular resource instances that is required by a workload. Created by a user (lifecycle managed manually, can be shared between different Pods) or for individual Pods by the control plane based on a ResourceClaimTemplate (automatic lifecycle, typically used by just one Pod).
  ResourceClaimTemplate:
    Description: Defines the spec and some meta data for creating ResourceClaims. Created by a user when deploying a workload.
  PodScheduling:
    Description: Used internally by the control plane and resource drivers to coordinate pod scheduling when ResourceClaims need to be allocated for a Pod.
```

TITLE: kubectl api-resources Command Options
DESCRIPTION: Detailed documentation for the available command-line options (flags) for `kubectl api-resources`, including their types, default values, and descriptions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubectl/generated/kubectl_api-resources/_index.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--api-group string
  Limit to resources in the specified API group.
--cached (bool)
  Use the cached list of resources if available.
--categories strings
  Limit to resources that belong to the specified categories.
-h, --help (bool)
  help for api-resources
--namespaced (bool) Default: true
  If false, non-namespaced resources will be returned, otherwise returning namespaced resources by default.
--no-headers (bool)
  When using the default or custom-column output format, don't print headers (default print headers).
-o, --output string
  Output format. One of: (wide, name).
--sort-by string
  If non-empty, sort list of resources using specified field. The field can be either 'name' or 'kind'.
--verbs strings
  Limit to resources that support the specified verbs.
```

TITLE: Kubernetes SelfSubjectAccessReview API Usage
DESCRIPTION: Describes the unique usage pattern of the Kubernetes SelfSubjectAccessReview API, which allows users to check their permissions. Unlike typical resources, it can only be 'created' (using the 'create' verb) to receive an immediate output of current access rights, and cannot be 'get' or 'list'ed.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2024-11-21-dynamic-kubernetes-api-server-for-cozystack/index.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
SelfSubjectAccessReview API:
  Purpose: Provides users with information about their permissions.
  Verbs:
    - create: Only verb supported to initiate a review and receive output.
    - get: Not supported.
    - list: Not supported.
  Behavior:
    - Creating a SelfSubjectAccessReview resource returns immediate information about current access.
```

TITLE: Migrate EndpointSlice from discovery.k8s.io/v1beta1 in Kubernetes v1.25
DESCRIPTION: This snippet describes the migration of EndpointSlice resources from the deprecated discovery.k8s.io/v1beta1 API version, removed in Kubernetes v1.25. It specifies the target API version and highlights changes in how node and zone information is represented.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
API Deprecated: discovery.k8s.io/v1beta1 (EndpointSlice)
Removed in Kubernetes: v1.25

Migration Target: discovery.k8s.io/v1 (available since v1.21)
Existing Objects: Accessible via new API

Notable Changes:
  Use per Endpoint nodeName field instead of deprecated topology[""kubernetes.io/hostname""] field.
  Use per Endpoint zone field instead of deprecated topology[""topology.kubernetes.io/zone""] field.
  topology is replaced with the deprecatedTopology field which is not writable in v1.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Kubernetes API: Single and Multi-Resource Operations
DESCRIPTION: Explains which Kubernetes API verbs operate on single resources exclusively and contrasts them with verbs that support multiple resources. It clarifies how clients interact with sets of resources using single-resource verbs.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_27

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Single Resource Verbs:
  - get
  - create
  - update
  - patch
  - delete
  - proxy
  Characteristics:
    - Support single resources only.
    - No support for submitting multiple resources together in an ordered or unordered list or transaction.
    - Clients (including kubectl) act on sets of resources by making a series of single-resource API requests and aggregating responses.

Multi Resource Verbs:
  - list: Allows getting multiple resources.
  - watch: Allows getting multiple resources.
  - deletecollection: Allows deleting multiple resources.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Install Kubernetes Hello Populator Example
DESCRIPTION: Deploys the example 'hello' populator, including its Custom Resource Definition (CRD) and deployment manifest, which demonstrates basic volume population functionality.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2021-08-30-volume-populators-alpha.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: terminal

TITLE: Examples of `gwctl` Commands for Gateway API Management
DESCRIPTION: This snippet provides various `bash` commands for `gwctl`, a command-line tool designed to manage and inspect Gateway API resources. It shows how to list policies and policy types, and describe resources like HTTPRoutes, Gateways, and GatewayClasses, including their effective policies across namespaces.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2023-11-28-Gateway-API-Future.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# List all policies in the cluster. This will also give the resource they bind
# to.
gwctl get policies -A
# List all available policy types.
gwctl get policycrds
# Describe all HTTPRoutes in namespace ns2. (Output includes effective policies)
gwctl describe httproutes -n ns2
# Describe a single HTTPRoute in the default namespace. (Output includes
# effective policies)
gwctl describe httproutes my-httproute-1
# Describe all Gateways across all namespaces. (Output includes effective
# policies)
gwctl describe gateways -A
# Describe a single GatewayClass. (Output includes effective policies)
gwctl describe gatewayclasses foo-com-external-gateway-class
```

TITLE: Configure Kubernetes API Server JWT Authentication with User Validation Failure
DESCRIPTION: This example showcases an `AuthenticationConfiguration` where `claimMappings` prefixes the username with 'system:', and a `userValidationRules` expression explicitly disallows usernames starting with 'system:'. Even if claim validation passes, the resulting `UserInfo` object will fail the user validation, leading to authentication rejection.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/access-authn-authz/authentication.md#_snippet_16

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: apiserver.config.k8s.io/v1beta1
kind: AuthenticationConfiguration
jwt:
- issuer:
    url: https://example.com
    audiences:
    - my-app
  claimValidationRules:
  - expression: 'claims.hd == ""example.com""'
    message: the hd claim must be set to example.com
  claimMappings:
    username:
      expression: '""system:"" + claims.username' # this will prefix the username with ""system:"" and will fail user validation.
    groups:
      expression: 'claims.roles.split("","")'
    uid:
      expression: 'claims.sub'
    extra:
    - key: 'example.com/tenant'
      valueExpression: 'claims.tenant'
  userValidationRules:
  - expression: ""!user.username.startsWith('system:')"" # the username will be system:foo and expression will evaluate to false, so validation will fail.
    message: 'username cannot used reserved system: prefix'
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
TOKEN=eyJhbGciOiJSUzI1NiIsImtpZCI6ImY3dF9tOEROWmFTQk1oWGw5QXZTWGhBUC04Y0JmZ0JVbFVpTG5oQkgxdXMiLCJ0eXAiOiJKV1QifQ.eyJhdWQiOiJrdWJlcm5ldGVzIiwiZXhwIjoxNzAzMjMyOTQ5LCJoZCI6ImV4YW1wbGUuY29tIiwiaWF0IjoxNzAxMTEzMTAxLCJpZGF0IjoxNzAxMTEzMTAxLCJpc3MiOiJodHRwczovL2V4YW1wbGUuY29tIiwianRpIjoiYjViMDY1MjM3MmNkMjBlMzQ1YjZmZGZmY2RjMjE4MWY0YWZkNmYyNTlhYWI0YjdlMzU4ODEyMzdkMjkyMjBiYyIsIm5iZiI6MTcwMTExMzEwMSwicm9sZXMiOiJ1c2VyLGFkbWluIiwic3ViIjoiYXV0aCIsInRlbmFudCI6IjcyZjk4OGJmLTg2ZjEtNDFhZi05MWFiLTJkN2NkMDExZGI0YSIsInVzZXJuYW1lIjoiZm9vIn0.FgPJBYLobo9jnbHreooBlvpgEcSPWnKfX6dc0IvdlRB-F0dCcgy91oCJeX_aBk-8zH5AKUXoFTlInfLCkPivMOJqMECA1YTrMUwt_IVqwb116AqihfByUYIIqzMjvUbthtbpIeHQm2fF0HbrUqa_Q0uaYwgy8mD807h7sBcUMjNd215ff_nFIHss-9zegH8GI1d9fiBf-g6zjkR1j987EP748khpQh9IxPjMJbSgG_uH5x80YFuqgEWwq-aYJPQxXX4FatP96a2EAn7wfPpGlPRt0HcBOvq5pCnudgCgfVgiOJiLr_7robQu4T1bis0W75VPEvwWtgFcLnvcQx0JWg

TITLE: Kubernetes API Deprecation Handling Behavior
DESCRIPTION: Describes the standard behavior of the Kubernetes API server when a request is made to a deprecated REST API endpoint, starting from Kubernetes v1.19. This includes the response headers, audit event annotations, and available Prometheus metrics for monitoring deprecated API usage.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-policy.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Kubernetes API Deprecation Handling (v1.19+):
  API Request to Deprecated Endpoint:
    Response Headers:
      - Warning: (RFC7234, Section 5.5) Indicates deprecation.
    Audit Event Annotation:
      - ""k8s.io/deprecated"": ""true"" (Added to audit event for the request)
    Prometheus Metrics:
      - apiserver_requested_deprecated_apis:
          Type: gauge
          Value: 1 (set when a deprecated API is requested)
          Labels:
            - group
            - version
            - resource
            - subresource
            - removed_release: Indicates the Kubernetes release when the API will be removed.
```

TITLE: Migrate FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration from flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta3 in Kubernetes v1.32
DESCRIPTION: This snippet details the migration of FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration resources from the deprecated flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta3 API version, which was removed in Kubernetes v1.32. It specifies the target API version and highlights changes to the nominalConcurrencyShares field.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
API Deprecated: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta3 (FlowSchema, PriorityLevelConfiguration)
Removed in Kubernetes: v1.32

Migration Target: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1 (available since v1.29)
Existing Objects: Accessible via new API

Notable Changes:
  PriorityLevelConfiguration.spec.limited.nominalConcurrencyShares:
    - Defaults to 30 when unspecified.
    - Explicit 0 value is not changed to 30.
```

TITLE: Migrate RBAC Resources API to rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
DESCRIPTION: The rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1beta1 API version for ClusterRole, ClusterRoleBinding, Role, and RoleBinding was removed in Kubernetes v1.22. Users must migrate to the rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1 API version, available since v1.8. All existing persisted objects are accessible via the new APIs without any notable changes.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_21

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Resource: ClusterRole, ClusterRoleBinding, Role, RoleBinding
Deprecated API: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1beta1 (Removed in v1.22)
New API: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1 (Available since v1.8)
Migration Notes:
  - All existing persisted objects are accessible via the new APIs
  - No notable changes
```

TITLE: Configure and List Pods with Go Kubernetes Client
DESCRIPTION: This Go code snippet demonstrates how to connect to a Kubernetes cluster using a kubeconfig file and list all pods. It utilizes the `k8s.io/client-go` library for API interaction and `k8s.io/apimachinery` for API types. The example shows how to build a client configuration from a kubeconfig path and then use the CoreV1 API to list pods.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/tasks/administer-cluster/access-cluster-api.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: golang
CODE:
```
package main

import (
  ""context""
  ""fmt""
  ""k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1""
  ""k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes""
  ""k8s.io/client-go/tools/clientcmd""
)

func main() {
  // uses the current context in kubeconfig
  // path-to-kubeconfig -- for example, /root/.kube/config
  config, _ := clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags("""", ""<path-to-kubeconfig>"")
  // creates the clientset
  clientset, _ := kubernetes.NewForConfig(config)
  // access the API to list pods
  pods, _ := clientset.CoreV1().Pods("""").List(context.TODO(), v1.ListOptions{})
  fmt.Printf(""There are %d pods in the cluster\n"", len(pods.Items))
}
```

TITLE: Waiting for Kubernetes API Server Health

TITLE: Migrate Deployment API to apps/v1
DESCRIPTION: The extensions/v1beta1, apps/v1beta1, and apps/v1beta2 API versions of Deployment were removed in Kubernetes v1.16. Users should migrate to the apps/v1 API version, available since v1.9. Key changes include the removal of `spec.rollbackTo`, `spec.selector` becoming required and immutable, and new default values for `spec.progressDeadlineSeconds`, `spec.revisionHistoryLimit`, `maxSurge`, and `maxUnavailable`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_26

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Resource: Deployment
Deprecated API: extensions/v1beta1, apps/v1beta1, apps/v1beta2 (Removed in v1.16)
New API: apps/v1 (Available since v1.9)
Migration Notes:
  - `spec.rollbackTo` is removed
  - `spec.selector` is now required and immutable after creation; use existing template labels as selector for seamless upgrades
  - `spec.progressDeadlineSeconds` now defaults to `600` seconds (was no deadline in `extensions/v1beta1`)
  - `spec.revisionHistoryLimit` now defaults to `10` (was `2` in `apps/v1beta1`, all in `extensions/v1beta1`)
  - `maxSurge` and `maxUnavailable` now default to `25%` (was `1` in `extensions/v1beta1`)
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API: List Request resourceVersionMatch Parameter Introduction
DESCRIPTION: Introduces the `resourceVersionMatch` parameter for Kubernetes `list` requests (from v1.19), explaining its interaction with `resourceVersion` and its benefits for performance and scalability. It also highlights the requirement to set `resourceVersionMatch` when `resourceVersion` is present and handling API servers unaware of the parameter.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_45

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
From version v1.19, Kubernetes API servers support the `resourceVersionMatch` parameter
on _list_ requests. If you set both `resourceVersion` and `resourceVersionMatch`, the
`resourceVersionMatch` parameter determines how the API server interprets
`resourceVersion`.

You should always set the `resourceVersionMatch` parameter when setting
`resourceVersion` on a **list** request. However, be prepared to handle the case
where the API server that responds is unaware of `resourceVersionMatch`
and ignores it.

Unless you have strong consistency requirements, using `resourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan` and
a known `resourceVersion` is preferable since it can achieve better performance and scalability
of your cluster than leaving `resourceVersion` and `resourceVersionMatch` unset, which requires
quorum read to be served.

Setting the `resourceVersionMatch` parameter without setting `resourceVersion` is not valid.
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API Object Read-only Metadata Fields Reference
DESCRIPTION: Provides a structured reference for the read-only metadata fields found in Kubernetes API objects, outlining their types, descriptions, and relevant API conventions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/common-definitions/object-meta.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
ObjectMetadata (Read-only Fields):
  creationTimestamp (Time):
    Description: Timestamp representing the server time when this object was created. Populated by the system. Read-only. Null for lists. Represented in RFC3339 form and UTC.
    More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#metadata
  deletionGracePeriodSeconds (int64):
    Description: Number of seconds allowed for this object to gracefully terminate before removal. Only set when deletionTimestamp is also set. May only be shortened. Read-only.
  deletionTimestamp (Time):
    Description: RFC 3339 date and time at which this resource will be deleted. Set by server when graceful deletion is requested. Blocks deletion if finalizers exist. Read-only.
    More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#metadata
  generation (int64):
    Description: A sequence number representing a specific generation of the desired state. Populated by the system. Read-only.
  resourceVersion (string):
    Description: An opaque value representing the internal version of this object. Used for optimistic concurrency, change detection, and watch operations. Populated by the system. Read-only.
    More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#concurrency-control-and-consistency
  selfLink (string):
    Description: Deprecated legacy read-only field. No longer populated by the system.
  uid (string):
    Description: Unique in time and space value for this object. Typically generated by the server on successful creation. Not allowed to change on PUT operations. Populated by the system. Read-only.
    More info: https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/overview/working-with-objects/names#uids

Type Definition:
  Time:
    Description: Wrapper around time.Time which supports correct marshaling to YAML and JSON. Wrappers are provided for many of the factory methods that the time package offers.
```

TITLE: Webhook Resources API Migration to admissionregistration.k8s.io/v1
DESCRIPTION: Outlines the deprecation of the admissionregistration.k8s.io/v1beta1 API version for MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration as of Kubernetes v1.22. It details several critical changes in default values and new requirements for fields like 'failurePolicy', 'matchPolicy', 'timeoutSeconds', 'sideEffects', 'admissionReviewVersions', and 'name' when migrating to the v1 API.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Webhook Resources API Migration:
  Deprecated: admissionregistration.k8s.io/v1beta1 (removed in v1.22)
  Migrate to: admissionregistration.k8s.io/v1 (available since v1.16)

  Notable changes in admissionregistration.k8s.io/v1:
    - webhooks[*].failurePolicy: default changed from 'Ignore' to 'Fail'
    - webhooks[*].matchPolicy: default changed from 'Exact' to 'Equivalent'
    - webhooks[*].timeoutSeconds: default changed from '30s' to '10s'
    - webhooks[*].sideEffects: default value removed, field required, only 'None' and 'NoneOnDryRun' permitted
    - webhooks[*].admissionReviewVersions: default value removed, field required (supported versions: 'v1', 'v1beta1')
    - webhooks[*].name: must be unique in the list
```

TITLE: Migrate DaemonSet API to apps/v1
DESCRIPTION: The extensions/v1beta1 and apps/v1beta2 API versions of DaemonSet were removed in Kubernetes v1.16. Users must migrate to the apps/v1 API version, available since v1.9. Notable changes include the removal of `spec.templateGeneration`, `spec.selector` becoming required and immutable, and `spec.updateStrategy.type` defaulting to `RollingUpdate`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_25

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Resource: DaemonSet
Deprecated API: extensions/v1beta1, apps/v1beta2 (Removed in v1.16)
New API: apps/v1 (Available since v1.9)
Migration Notes:
  - `spec.templateGeneration` is removed
  - `spec.selector` is now required and immutable after creation; use existing template labels as selector for seamless upgrades
  - `spec.updateStrategy.type` now defaults to `RollingUpdate` (was `OnDelete` in `extensions/v1beta1`)
```

TITLE: Generate Kubernetes API Reference Links from Page Metadata
DESCRIPTION: This Go template iterates through `api_metadata` defined in a page's front matter (e.g., `apiVersion`, `kind`). It searches for corresponding API reference pages within the `docs/reference/kubernetes-api/` directory, constructs a markdown link for each match, and stores these links for later use. It handles overrides for link text and ensures only valid metadata is processed.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/layouts/partials/docs/api-reference-links.html#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: Go Template
CODE:
```
{{- $apiReferenceMetaLinks := slice -}}
{{- $apiReferenceText := T ""api_reference_title"" -}}
{{ $.Store.Delete ""apiReferenceMetaLinks"" }}
{{ $.Store.Delete ""pageApiReferenceLinksMap"" }}
{{- $ignoreCondition := (printf ""%T"" .Page.Params.api_metadata | eq ""[]interface {}"") -}}
{{- if and .Page.Params.api_metadata $ignoreCondition (not .Page.Params.simple_list) -}}
{{- range $metadata := .Page.Params.api_metadata -}}
{{- $apiVersion := $metadata.apiVersion -}}
{{- $kind := $metadata.kind -}}
{{- $version := $apiVersion -}}
{{- $linkText := $metadata.override_link_text | default $kind -}}
{{- $apiRefBaseDir := ""docs/reference/kubernetes-api/"" -}}
{{- $apiRefSections := site.GetPage ""section"" $apiRefBaseDir -}}
{{- range $apiRefSection := $apiRefSections.Sections -}}
{{- $apiRefDir := $apiRefSection.RelPermalink -}}
{{- $fragmentApiRefDir := split $apiRefDir ""/docs"" -}}
{{- $apiRefDir := printf ""/docs%s"" (index ($fragmentApiRefDir) 1) -}}
{{- $apiReferenceFiles := site.GetPage $apiRefDir -}}
{{- range $apiRefFile := $apiReferenceFiles.RegularPages -}}
{{- $apiRefFileDirPath:= printf ""/%s"" $apiRefFile.File.Dir -}}
{{- if and (ne $apiRefFile.Section """") (in $apiRefFileDirPath $apiRefDir) -}}
{{- with $apiRefFile.Params.api_metadata -}}
{{- if and (eq .kind $kind) (eq .apiVersion $version) -}}
{{- $link := printf ""[%s %s](%s)"" $apiRefFile.Permalink $linkText $apiReferenceText -}}
{{- $apiReferenceMetaLinks = $apiReferenceMetaLinks | append $link -}}
{{- $.Store.SetInMap ""pageApiReferenceLinksMap"" $kind $link -}}
{{- end -}}
{{- end -}}
{{- end -}}
{{- end -}}
{{- end -}}
{{- end -}}
{{- end -}}
{{- if gt (len $apiReferenceMetaLinks) 0 -}}
{{ $.Store.Add ""apiReferenceMetaLinks"" $apiReferenceMetaLinks }}
{{- end -}}
```

TITLE: Comparing GitHub Workflows for Kubernetes Contributions
DESCRIPTION: This snippet highlights the discrepancy between two common GitHub workflows for Kubernetes contributions: one recommended by SIG Docs and another by the Kubernetes Community Contributor Guide. It shows the commands for each approach to creating a local branch.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2019-11-05-grokkin-the-docs.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: git
CODE:
```
# Workflow 1: SIG Docs GitHub process (recommended for local branch creation)
# Based on upstream/master directly
git fetch upstream
git checkout -b my-feature-branch upstream/master

# Workflow 2: Kubernetes Community Contributor Guide (advocated for updating fork first)
# 1. Update your fork from upstream
git fetch upstream
git checkout master # or main
git rebase upstream/master # or upstream/main
git push origin master # or main
# 2. Create a local branch based on your updated fork
git checkout -b my-feature-branch
```

self.foo == oldSelf.foo
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
oldSelf != 'bar' || self == 'bar'
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
!has(oldSelf.field) || has(self.field)
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
self.all(element, element in oldSelf)
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
oldSelf != 'X' || self in ['A', 'B']
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
self >= oldSelf
```

TITLE: Perform Background Cascading Deletion of Kubernetes Deployment

Examples are provided for both `kubectl` command-line usage and direct interaction with the Kubernetes API via `curl` after starting a local proxy.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/tasks/administer-cluster/use-cascading-deletion.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: shell
CODE:
```

```

LANGUAGE: shell
CODE:
```
kubectl proxy --port=8080
```

LANGUAGE: shell
CODE:
```
curl -X DELETE localhost:8080/apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments/nginx-deployment \
    -d '{""kind"":""DeleteOptions"",""apiVersion"":""v1"",""propagationPolicy"":""Background""}' \
    -H ""Content-Type: application/json""
```

TITLE: Create a Kubernetes Ingress Object
DESCRIPTION: API endpoint and parameters for creating a new Kubernetes Ingress resource within a specified namespace.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/service-resources/ingress-v1.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
HTTP Request:
  POST /apis/networking.k8s.io/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/ingresses

Parameters:
  - namespace (in path): string, required
    Description: The namespace for the Ingress resource.
  - body: Ingress, required
    Description: The Ingress object to create.
  - dryRun (in query): string
    Description: If 'true', then the request is not actually performed.
  - fieldManager (in query): string
    Description: Name of the field manager for the API request.
  - fieldValidation (in query): string
    Description: Field validation behavior.
  - pretty (in query): string
    Description: If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.

Response:
  - 200 (Ingress): OK
  - 201 (Ingress): Created
  - 202 (Ingress): Accepted
  - 401: Unauthorized
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Kubernetes Watch: Start at Exact Semantic
DESCRIPTION: Details the 'Start at Exact' semantic for Kubernetes `watch` operations. The watch begins precisely at the provided `resourceVersion` without generating synthetic 'Added' events, assuming the client already possesses the initial state.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_54

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Start a **watch** at an exact resource version. The watch events are for all changes
after the provided resource version. Unlike ""Get State and Start at Most Recent""
and ""Get State and Start at Any"", the **watch** is not started with synthetic
""Added"" events for the provided resource version. The client is assumed to already
have the initial state at the starting resource version since the client provided
the resource version.
```

TITLE: kubectl proxy Command Usage and Examples
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates various ways to use the `kubectl proxy` command, including its general syntax, proxying the entire API, serving static files, changing API prefixes, and specifying custom ports.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubectl/generated/kubectl_proxy/_index.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
kubectl proxy [--port=PORT] [--www=static-dir] [--www-prefix=prefix] [--api-prefix=prefix]
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# To proxy all of the Kubernetes API and nothing else
kubectl proxy --api-prefix=/
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# To proxy only part of the Kubernetes API and also some static files
# You can get pods info with 'curl localhost:8001/api/v1/pods'
kubectl proxy --www=/my/files --www-prefix=/static/ --api-prefix=/api/
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# To proxy the entire Kubernetes API at a different root
# You can get pods info with 'curl localhost:8001/custom/api/v1/pods'
kubectl proxy --api-prefix=/custom/
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Run a proxy to the Kubernetes API server on port 8011, serving static content from ./local/www/
kubectl proxy --port=8011 --www=./local/www/
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Run a proxy to the Kubernetes API server on an arbitrary local port
# The chosen port for the server will be output to stdout
kubectl proxy --port=0
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Run a proxy to the Kubernetes API server, changing the API prefix to k8s-api
# This makes e.g. the pods API available at localhost:8001/k8s-api/v1/pods/
kubectl proxy --api-prefix=/k8s-api
```
