TITLE: Querying Deprecated Kubernetes API Requests with kubectl and jq
DESCRIPTION: This `kubectl` command, piped through `prom2json` and `jq`, identifies which deprecated APIs have been requested from the current API server instance by filtering the `apiserver_requested_deprecated_apis` metric. The output shows the API group, version, resource, subresource, and the Kubernetes release in which the API will be removed.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2020-09-03-warnings/index.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
kubectl get --raw /metrics | prom2json | jq '
  .[] | select(.name==""apiserver_requested_deprecated_apis"").metrics[].labels
'
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Kubernetes Protobuf Wrapper IDL
DESCRIPTION: Defines the Protobuf Interface Definition Language (IDL) for the `Unknown` and `TypeMeta` messages used in Kubernetes' custom Protobuf envelope wrapper. This IDL specifies the structure of the wrapper message, including fields for type metadata, raw serialized object data, content encoding, and content type.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
A four byte magic number prefix:
  Bytes 0-3: ""k8s\x00"" [0x6b, 0x38, 0x73, 0x00]

An encoded Protobuf message with the following IDL:
  message Unknown {
    // typeMeta should have the string values for ""kind"" and ""apiVersion"" as set on the JSON object
    optional TypeMeta typeMeta = 1;

    // raw will hold the complete serialized object in protobuf. See the protobuf definitions in the client libraries for a given kind.
    optional bytes raw = 2;

    // contentEncoding is encoding used for the raw data. Unspecified means no encoding.
    optional string contentEncoding = 3;

    // contentType is the serialization method used to serialize 'raw'. Unspecified means application/vnd.kubernetes.protobuf and is usually
    // omitted.
    optional string contentType = 4;
  }

  message TypeMeta {
    // apiVersion is the group/version for this type
    optional string apiVersion = 1;
    // kind is the name of the object schema. A protobuf definition should exist for this object.
    optional string kind = 2;
  }
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API Server Encryption Configuration (AES-CBC)
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet illustrates a typical `EncryptionConfiguration` for the Kubernetes API server, where `secrets` are encrypted at rest using the `aescbc` provider. This configuration serves as an example of an existing setup before disabling encryption.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/tasks/administer-cluster/decrypt-data.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
---
apiVersion: apiserver.config.k8s.io/v1
kind: EncryptionConfiguration
resources:
  - resources:
      - secrets
    providers:
      - aescbc:
          keys:
            # Do not use this (invalid) example key for encryption
            - name: example
              secret: 2KfZgdiq2K0g2YrYpyDYs9mF2LPZhQ==
```

TITLE: Kubernetes DaemonSet API Object Definition
DESCRIPTION: Defines the structure and fields for the Kubernetes DaemonSet API object, including its metadata, desired specification, and current status, along with relevant API conventions.

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
apiVersion: apps/v1
import: k8s.io/api/apps/v1

DaemonSet:
  description: DaemonSet represents the configuration of a daemon set.
  properties:
    apiVersion:
      type: string
      value: apps/v1
    kind:
      type: string
      value: DaemonSet
    metadata:
      type: ObjectMeta
      description: Standard object's metadata. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#metadata
    spec:
      type: DaemonSetSpec
      description: The desired behavior of this daemon set. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#spec-and-status
    status:
      type: DaemonSetStatus
      description: The current status of this daemon set. This data may be out of date by some window of time. Populated by the system. Read-only. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#spec-and-status
```

TITLE: Kueue Interaction with Kubernetes Job API
DESCRIPTION: Kueue influences the behavior of Kubernetes Jobs by utilizing specific fields within the Job API. This allows Kueue to control when a job starts or stops and to modify its scheduling directives before execution, delegating actual pod-to-node scheduling to kube-scheduler.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2022-10-04-introducing-kueue.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Kubernetes Job API Interactions:
  - Suspend Field:
      Purpose: Allows Kueue to signal the job-controller to start or stop a Job.
      Path: .spec.suspend (conceptual usage)
  - Mutable Scheduling Directives:
      Purpose: Enables Kueue to update a Job's .spec.template.spec.nodeSelector before starting the Job.
      Path: .spec.template.spec.nodeSelector (conceptual usage)
```

TITLE: CSI Driver Group Snapshot API Implementation Requirements

    Location: Query
  - Name: gracePeriodSeconds
    Type: integer
    Location: Query
  - Name: ignoreStoreReadErrorWithClusterBreakingPotential
    Type: boolean
    Location: Query
  - Name: labelSelector
    Type: string
    Location: Query
  - Name: limit
    Type: integer
    Location: Query
  - Name: pretty
    Type: string
    Location: Query
  - Name: propagationPolicy
    Type: string
    Location: Query
  - Name: resourceVersion
    Type: string
    Location: Query
  - Name: resourceVersionMatch
    Type: string
    Location: Query
  - Name: sendInitialEvents
    Type: boolean
    Location: Query
  - Name: timeoutSeconds
    Type: integer
    Location: Query

Responses:
  - Code: 200
    Status: OK
    Returns: Status
  - Code: 401
    Status: Unauthorized
    Returns: None
```

TITLE: Hugo Tabs Shortcode API Documentation
DESCRIPTION: Documents the available parameters for the `tabs` and `tab` shortcodes in Hugo, including `name`, `codelang`, and `include`, along with usage notes for markdown content and self-closing syntax.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/contribute/style/hugo-shortcodes/index.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
tabs shortcode parameters:
  - name: The name as shown on the tab.
  - codelang: Code language for highlighting inner content of a `tab` shortcode.
  - include: The file to include in the tab.
    - If in a Hugo leaf bundle, file is looked up in the bundle.
    - Otherwise, looked up relative to the current page.
    - Requires self-closing syntax: `{{</* tab name=""Content File #1"" include=""example1"" /*/>}}`
    - Language derived from `codelang` or file name; non-content files are code-highlighted by default.
  - Markdown inner content: Must use `%`-delimiter.
    - Example: `{{%/* tab name=""Tab 1"" %}}This is **markdown**{{% /tab */%}}`
  - Combinations: Different variations can be combined within a tab set.
Note: The tab `name` in a `tabs` definition must be unique within a content page.
```

TITLE: Enable Runtime Config Emulation Forward Compatibility
DESCRIPTION: When set to true, this flag allows APIs enabled via `--runtime-config` to be installed even if they are introduced after the emulation version. If false, the server will fail to start if such APIs are enabled. This flag can only be true if the emulation version is lower than the binary version.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/command-line-tools-reference/kube-apiserver.md#_snippet_109

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--runtime-config-emulation-forward-compatible
  Description: If true, APIs identified by group/version that are enabled in the --runtime-config flag will be installed even if it is introduced after the emulation version. If false, server would fail to start if any APIs identified by group/version that are enabled in the --runtime-config flag are introduced after the emulation version. Can only be set to true if the emulation version is lower than the binary version.
```

TITLE: CRD Annotations for Server-side Apply
DESCRIPTION: This section outlines new annotations available for Custom Resource Definitions (CRDs) that enhance Server-side Apply behavior. It covers annotations for specifying default values for fields and controlling the atomicity of maps and structs, providing both Golang and OpenAPI extension syntax for each.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2021-08-06-server-side-apply-ga.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
CRD Annotations for Server-side Apply:
  Defaulting:
    Description: Values for fields that appliers do not express explicit interest in should be defaulted. This prevents an applier from unintentionally owning a defaulted field that might cause conflicts with other appliers.
    Golang: +default=<value>
    OpenAPI extension: default: <value>

  Atomic for maps and structs:
    Maps:
      Description: By default maps are granular. A different manager is able to manage each map entry. They can also be configured to be atomic such that a single manager owns the entire map.
      Golang: +mapType=granular/atomic
      OpenAPI extension: x-kubernetes-map-type: granular/atomic
    Structs:
      Description: By default structs are granular and a separate applier may own each field. For certain kinds of structs, atomicity may be desired, commonly seen in small coordinate-like structs.
      Golang: +structType=granular/atomic
      OpenAPI extension: x-kubernetes-map-type:atomic/granular
```

TITLE: Migrate FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration from flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta2 in Kubernetes v1.29
DESCRIPTION: This snippet outlines the migration path for FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration resources from the deprecated flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta2 API version, removed in Kubernetes v1.29. It provides two migration targets and details field renames and default value changes for each.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/deprecation-guide.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
API Deprecated: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta2 (FlowSchema, PriorityLevelConfiguration)
Removed in Kubernetes: v1.29

Migration Target 1: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1 (available since v1.29)
Existing Objects: Accessible via new API
Notable Changes:
  PriorityLevelConfiguration.spec.limited.assuredConcurrencyShares renamed to spec.limited.nominalConcurrencyShares.
  nominalConcurrencyShares defaults to 30 when unspecified; explicit 0 is not changed to 30.

Migration Target 2: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta3 (available since v1.26)
Existing Objects: Accessible via new API
Notable Changes:
  PriorityLevelConfiguration.spec.limited.assuredConcurrencyShares renamed to spec.limited.nominalConcurrencyShares.
```

TITLE: Kubernetes Workload API: Deployment

SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/concepts/workloads/controllers/_index.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Deployment:
  Description: Most common way to run an application on your cluster.
  Purpose: Manages stateless application workloads.
  Characteristics:
    - Any Pod in the Deployment is interchangeable and can be replaced.
    - Replaces the legacy ReplicationController API.
    - Indirectly uses ReplicaSet.
```

TITLE: API Removal: FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration v1beta3
DESCRIPTION: The `flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta3` API version for FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration has been removed in Kubernetes v1.32. Users should migrate to the `flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1` API version, available since v1.29. Existing persisted objects are accessible via the new API, with notable changes in `spec.limited.nominalConcurrencyShares` field defaulting behavior.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2024-12-11-Kubernetes-v1-32-Release/index.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
API Removal in Kubernetes v1.32:
- `flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta3` API version of FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration has been removed.
- Recommended migration: Use `flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1` API version (available since v1.29).
- All existing persisted objects are accessible via the new API.
- Notable changes in `flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta3`:
  - PriorityLevelConfiguration `spec.limited.nominalConcurrencyShares` field only defaults to 30 when unspecified.
  - An explicit value of 0 is not changed to 30.
```

TITLE: kubectl create namespace command options
DESCRIPTION: Detailed documentation for all available command-line options that can be used with `kubectl create namespace`, including their types, default values, and comprehensive descriptions of their functionality.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubectl/generated/kubectl_create/kubectl_create_namespace.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Option: --allow-missing-template-keys (Default: true)
  Description: If true, ignore any errors in templates when a field or map key is missing in the template. Only applies to golang and jsonpath output formats.
Option: --dry-run string[=""unchanged""] (Default: ""none"")
  Description: Must be ""none"", ""server"", or ""client"". If client strategy, only print the object that would be sent, without sending it. If server strategy, submit server-side request without persisting the resource.
Option: --field-manager string (Default: ""kubectl-create"")
  Description: Name of the manager used to track field ownership.
Option: -h, --help
  Description: help for namespace
Option: -o, --output string
  Description: Output format. One of: (json, yaml, name, go-template, go-template-file, template, templatefile, jsonpath, jsonpath-as-json, jsonpath-file).
Option: --save-config
  Description: If true, the configuration of current object will be saved in its annotation. Otherwise, the annotation will be unchanged. This flag is useful when you want to perform kubectl apply on this object in the future.
Option: --show-managed-fields
  Description: If true, keep the managedFields when printing objects in JSON or YAML format.
Option: --template string
  Description: Template string or path to template file to use when -o=go-template, -o=go-template-file. The template format is golang templates [http://golang.org/pkg/text/template/#pkg-overview].
Option: --validate string[=""strict""] (Default: ""strict"")
  Description: Must be one of: strict (or true), warn, ignore (or false). ""true"" or ""strict"" will use a schema to validate the input and fail the request if invalid. It will perform server side validation if ServerSideFieldValidation is enabled on the api-server, but will fall back to less reliable client-side validation if not. ""warn"" will warn about unknown or duplicate fields without blocking the request if server-side field validation is enabled on the API server, and behave as ""ignore"" otherwise. ""false"" or ""ignore"" will not perform any schema validation, silently dropping any unknown or duplicate fields.
```

TITLE: Kubernetes ReplicaSet API Object Definition

TITLE: kubectl annotate Usage Examples
DESCRIPTION: Provides practical examples demonstrating how to use `kubectl annotate` to add, modify, overwrite, and remove annotations on various Kubernetes resources like pods, including scenarios for updating all resources in a namespace or performing conditional updates based on resource versions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubectl/generated/kubectl_annotate/_index.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: shell
CODE:
```
  # Update pod 'foo' with the annotation 'description' and the value 'my frontend'
  # If the same annotation is set multiple times, only the last value will be applied
  kubectl annotate pods foo description='my frontend'
  
  # Update a pod identified by type and name in ""pod.json""
  kubectl annotate -f pod.json description='my frontend'
  
  # Update pod 'foo' with the annotation 'description' and the value 'my frontend running nginx', overwriting any existing value
  kubectl annotate --overwrite pods foo description='my frontend running nginx'
  
  # Update all pods in the namespace
  kubectl annotate pods --all description='my frontend running nginx'
  
  # Update pod 'foo' only if the resource is unchanged from version 1
  kubectl annotate pods foo description='my frontend running nginx' --resource-version=1
  
  # Update pod 'foo' by removing an annotation named 'description' if it exists
  # Does not require the --overwrite flag
  kubectl annotate pods foo description-
```

TITLE: Cluster API Resource Overview and Relationships
DESCRIPTION: This section outlines the core resources used in Cluster API for deploying and managing Kubernetes clusters, including the Cluster resource, control plane and infrastructure resources, and MachineDeployment for node management. It details the purpose and interdependencies of these resources, along with the set of resources required for a new cluster deployment.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2024-04-05-diy-create-your-own-cloud-with-kubernetes-part-3/index.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Cluster API Resources:
  Cluster:
    Description: Primary object, acts as the parent for all other Cluster API resources.
    References:
      - Control Plane Resource (e.g., KamajiControlPlane)
      - Infrastructure Resource (e.g., KubevirtCluster)

  Control Plane Resource:
    Description: Manages the Kubernetes control plane. Its 'kind' depends on the specific provider.
    Example: KamajiControlPlane (when using Kamaji)

  Infrastructure Resource:
    Description: Describes the cluster configuration within a specific infrastructure provider. Its 'kind' depends on the specific provider.
    Example: KubevirtCluster (when using KubeVirt)

  MachineDeployment:
    Description: Describes a group of nodes (physical servers or virtual machines). Functions similarly to Kubernetes Deployment, ReplicaSet, and Pod for declarative node management and automatic scaling.
    References:
      - Machine Template (e.g., KubevirtMachineTemplate)
      - Cloud-init Config Template (e.g., KubeadmConfigTemplate)

  KubevirtMachineTemplate:
    Description: A template resource responsible for generating virtual machines within KubeVirt.

  KubeadmConfigTemplate:
    Description: A template resource responsible for generating tokens and cloud-init configurations for nodes.

  KamajiControlPlane:
    Description: A resource specifically for managing the Kubernetes control plane when using Kamaji.

Required Resources for New Cluster Deployment (using Cluster API, Kamaji, KubeVirt):
  - A general Cluster resource
  - A KamajiControlPlane resource (for Kamaji-operated control plane)
  - A KubevirtCluster resource (for KubeVirt cluster configuration)
  - A KubevirtMachineTemplate resource (for virtual machine templates)
  - A KubeadmConfigTemplate resource (for generating tokens and cloud-init)
  - At least one MachineDeployment (to create worker nodes)
```

TITLE: Deploying a PodResources Monitoring Agent DaemonSet
DESCRIPTION: Example Kubernetes DaemonSet manifest for a hypothetical monitoring agent that consumes the podresources API. It demonstrates how to mount the kubelet's pod-resources directory into the container to ensure persistent socket access after kubelet restarts.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2023-08-23-kubelet-podresources-api-ga.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: podresources-monitoring-app
  namespace: monitoring
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      name: podresources-monitoring
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        name: podresources-monitoring
    spec:
      containers:
      - args:
        - --podresources-socket=unix:///host-podresources/kubelet.sock
        command:
        - /bin/podresources-monitor
        image: podresources-monitor:latest  # just for an example
        volumeMounts:
        - mountPath: /host-podresources
          name: host-podresources
      serviceAccountName: podresources-monitor
      volumes:
      - hostPath:
          path: /var/lib/kubelet/pod-resources
          type: Directory
        name: host-podresources
```

TITLE: Configure HTTPRoute for CORS Filtering
DESCRIPTION: This YAML example demonstrates how to configure a `HTTPRoute` resource to enable Cross-Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) filtering. It defines a rule for a specific path prefix (`/resource/foo`) and applies a CORS filter that allows all origins, specific HTTP methods (GET, HEAD, POST), and a set of standard HTTP headers. This configuration ensures that the Gateway returns appropriate CORS response headers.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2025-06-02-gateway-api-v1.3/index.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: gateway.networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: HTTPRoute
metadata:
  name: http-route-cors
spec:
  parentRefs:
  - name: http-gateway
  rules:
  - matches:
    - path:
        type: PathPrefix
        value: /resource/foo
    filters:
    - cors:
      - type: CORS
        allowOrigins:
        - ""*""
        allowMethods:
        - GET
        - HEAD
        - POST
        allowHeaders:
        - Accept
        - Accept-Language
        - Content-Language
        - Content-Type
        - Range
    backendRefs:
    - kind: Service
      name: http-route-cors
      port: 80
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API Server Health Endpoints Reference
DESCRIPTION: Comprehensive reference for the Kubernetes API server's health, liveness, and readiness endpoints, including their usage, parameters, and individual check capabilities. These endpoints indicate the current status of the API server.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/health-checks.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
API Endpoints:

- /healthz (Deprecated since v1.16)
  Description: Indicates overall API server health.
  Parameters:
    - verbose (optional): boolean
      Description: If present, prints all checks and their status. Intended for human debugging.
  Response:
    - HTTP Status Code 200: Indicates healthy.

- /livez
  Description: Indicates API server liveness. Can be used with `--livez-grace-period` flag for startup duration.
  Parameters:
    - verbose (optional): boolean
      Description: If present, prints all checks and their status. Intended for human debugging.
    - exclude (optional): string
      Description: Comma-separated list of check names to exclude from the status report.
  Response:
    - HTTP Status Code 200: Indicates live.
    - Verbose Output Format: ""[+]<check-name> ok"" or ""[+]<check-name> excluded: ok""

- /readyz
  Description: Indicates API server readiness. Can be used with `--shutdown-delay-duration` flag for graceful shutdown.
  Parameters:
    - verbose (optional): boolean
      Description: If present, prints all checks and their status. Intended for human debugging.
    - exclude (optional): string
      Description: Comma-separated list of check names to exclude from the status report.
  Response:
    - HTTP Status Code 200: Indicates ready.
    - Verbose Output Format: ""[+]<check-name> ok"" or ""[+]<check-name> excluded: ok""

- /livez/<healthcheck-name> (Alpha Feature)
  Description: Checks the liveness of a specific individual health check.
  Parameters:
    - <healthcheck-name>: string (Path Parameter)
      Description: The name of the individual check to query (e.g., ""etcd"", ""ping""). Names can be discovered using the `verbose` flag on `/livez`.
  Response:
    - HTTP Status Code 200: Indicates the specific check is live.

- /readyz/<healthcheck-name> (Alpha Feature)
  Description: Checks the readiness of a specific individual health check.
  Parameters:
    - <healthcheck-name>: string (Path Parameter)
      Description: The name of the individual check to query.
  Response:
    - HTTP Status Code 200: Indicates the specific check is ready.
```

TITLE: Overview of Kubernetes Extension Mechanisms

--as string
  Username to impersonate for the operation. User could be a regular user or a service account in a namespace.

--as-uid string
  UID to impersonate for the operation.

  Default cache directory

  Path to a cert file for the certificate authority

  Path to a client certificate file for TLS
--client-key string
  Path to a client key file for TLS

  The name of the kubeconfig cluster to use

  The name of the kubeconfig context to use

--default-unreachable-toleration-seconds int Default: 300
  Indicates the tolerationSeconds of the toleration for unreachable:NoExecute that is added by default to every pod that does not already have such a toleration.

  Require server version to match client version

  If present, the namespace scope for this CLI request

  Password for basic authentication to the API server

  Name of profile to capture. One of (none|cpu|heap|goroutine|threadcreate|block|mutex)
--profile-output string Default: ""profile.pprof""
  Name of the file to write the profile to
--request-timeout string Default: ""0""
  The length of time to wait before giving up on a single server request. Non-zero values should contain a corresponding time unit (e.g. 1s, 2m, 3h). A value of zero means don't timeout requests.
-s, --server string
  The address and port of the Kubernetes API server
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Kubernetes Label Selector API Specification (APIDOC)
DESCRIPTION: Detailed specification of Kubernetes Label Selectors as used in the API. Covers the syntax and behavior of equality-based (`=`, `==`, `!=`) and set-based (`in`, `notin`, `exists`, `!exists`) requirements, and how multiple requirements are combined using an implicit AND logic.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/ko/docs/concepts/overview/working-with-objects/labels.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Label Selectors:
  Purpose: Identify objects based on attached labels.
  Types:
    1. Equality-based Requirements:
      - Operators: `=`, `==` (equality), `!=` (inequality)
      - Syntax: `key=value`, `key==value`, `key!=value`
      - Example: `environment=production`, `tier!=frontend`
    2. Set-based Requirements:
      - Operators: `in`, `notin`, `exists` (key only), `!exists` (key only)
      - Syntax: `key in (value1, value2)`, `key notin (value1, value2)`, `key`, `!key`
      - Example: `environment in (production, qa)`, `tier notin (frontend, backend)`, `partition`, `!partition`
  Combination Logic:
    - Multiple requirements are separated by commas (`,`).
    - Commas act as an implicit logical AND (&&) operator.
    - Example: `environment=production,tier!=frontend`
  Constraints:
    - No logical OR (||) operator supported for selector requirements.
    - For some API types (e.g., ReplicaSet), label selectors for two instances within a namespace must not overlap.
```

TITLE: Continue Chunked Pod Listing in Kubernetes
DESCRIPTION: This HTTP request continues a previous chunked listing of pods by passing the `continue` token received from the prior response. It fetches the next set of 500 pods, and the response provides a new `continue` token for further pagination.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_18

LANGUAGE: http
CODE:
```
GET /api/v1/pods?limit=500&continue=ENCODED_CONTINUE_TOKEN
---
200 OK
Content-Type: application/json

{
  ""kind"": ""PodList"",
  ""apiVersion"": ""v1"",
  ""metadata"": {
    ""resourceVersion"":""10245"",
    ""continue"": ""ENCODED_CONTINUE_TOKEN_2"",
    ""remainingItemCount"": 253,
    ...
  },
  ""items"": [...] // returns pods 501-1000
}
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API: Create ReplicationController
DESCRIPTION: Documents the parameters for creating a new Kubernetes ReplicationController object within a specified namespace. This operation allows for dry runs and field management.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/workload-resources/replication-controller-v1.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
HTTP Method: POST
Path: /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers
Parameters:
  - namespace (in path): string, required
    Description: The namespace to create the ReplicationController in.
  - body: ReplicationController, required
    Description: The ReplicationController object to create.
  - dryRun (in query): string
    Description: When present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted.
  - fieldManager (in query): string
    Description: FieldManager indicates the name of the actor that is making these changes.
  - fieldValidation (in query): string
    Description: FieldValidation specifies the validation strategy for the request.
  - pretty (in query): string
    Description: If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.
```

TITLE: Specify Machine-Readable Validation Failure Reasons in Kubernetes
DESCRIPTION: This example shows how to use the `reason` field in `x-kubernetes-validations` to provide a machine-readable error code for validation failures. The specified reason (e.g., 'FieldValueInvalid') influences the HTTP status code returned to the API caller, offering more precise error handling.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/tasks/extend-kubernetes/custom-resources/custom-resource-definitions.md#_snippet_55

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
x-kubernetes-validations:
- rule: ""self.x <= self.maxLimit""
  reason: ""FieldValueInvalid""
```

TITLE: Example Kubernetes Webhook Token Authentication Configuration
DESCRIPTION: This YAML configuration file, formatted like a kubeconfig, defines the settings for a Kubernetes API server's webhook token authentication. It specifies the remote authentication service details (CA, server URL) and the client certificate/key for the API server to use when communicating with the webhook.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/access-authn-authz/authentication.md#_snippet_21

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
# Kubernetes API version
apiVersion: v1
# kind of the API object
kind: Config
# clusters refers to the remote service.
clusters:
  - name: name-of-remote-authn-service
    cluster:
      certificate-authority: /path/to/ca.pem         # CA for verifying the remote service.
      server: https://authn.example.com/authenticate # URL of remote service to query. 'https' recommended for production.

# users refers to the API server's webhook configuration.
users:
  - name: name-of-api-server
    user:
      client-certificate: /path/to/cert.pem # cert for the webhook plugin to use
      client-key: /path/to/key.pem          # key matching the cert
```

TITLE: Common Parameters for Kubernetes API Operations
DESCRIPTION: This section outlines a set of common parameters frequently utilized across various Kubernetes API endpoints. These parameters facilitate filtering, pagination, and watch functionality, providing consistent control over API requests.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/workload-resources/stateful-set-v1.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameters:
  - namespace (in path): string, required
    Description: The namespace for the request.
  - allowWatchBookmarks (in query): boolean
    Description: Requests watch events with type ""BOOKMARK"".
  - continue (in query): string
    Description: Used to indicate that the server should return the next page of data.
  - fieldSelector (in query): string
    Description: A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields.
  - labelSelector (in query): string
    Description: A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their labels.
  - limit (in query): integer
    Description: Maximum number of items to return.
  - pretty (in query): string
    Description: If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.
  - resourceVersion (in query): string
    Description: Sets a constraint on what resource versions a request may be served from.
  - resourceVersionMatch (in query): string
    Description: Determines how the resourceVersion is applied to list calls.
  - sendInitialEvents (in query): boolean
    Description: `sendInitialEvents=true` may be set together with `watch=true` to get current state.
  - timeoutSeconds (in query): integer
    Description: Timeout for the list/watch call in seconds.
  - watch (in query): boolean
    Description: Watch for changes to the described resources and return events for each change.
```

TITLE: Configure HTTPRoute Retry Support
DESCRIPTION: Gateway API 1.2.0 introduces experimental support for counted HTTPRoute retries. This configuration example shows how to set up an HTTPRoute to retry requests to the `/face` path up to 3 times with a 500ms delay between retries, specifically for HTTP 5xx status codes.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2024-11-21-gateway-api-v1-2/index.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: gateway.networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: HTTPRoute
metadata:
  name: face-with-retries
  namespace: faces
spec:
  parentRefs:
    - name: my-gateway
      kind: Gateway
      port: 80
  rules:
  - matches:
    - path:
        type: PathPrefix
        value: /face
    backendRefs:
    - name: face
      port: 80
    retry:
      codes: [ 500, 502, 503, 504 ]
      attempts: 3
      backoff: 500ms
```

TITLE: Kubernetes v1.32 API Removal: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta3
DESCRIPTION: The `flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1beta3` API version for FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration has been removed in Kubernetes v1.32. Users must migrate their manifests and client software to use the `flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1` API version, which has been available since v1.29. Existing persisted objects are accessible via the new API.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2024-11-08-kubernetes-1.32-sneak-peek.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
API Removal:
  Group: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io
  Version: v1beta3
  Kind: FlowSchema, PriorityLevelConfiguration
  Removed In: Kubernetes v1.32
  Replacement API:
    Group: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io
    Version: v1
    Availability: Since Kubernetes v1.29
  Migration Notes:
    - All existing persisted objects are accessible via the new API.
    - Notable changes in v1beta3 (compared to v1):
      - PriorityLevelConfiguration.spec.limited.nominalConcurrencyShares:
        - Defaults to 30 only when unspecified.
        - An explicit value of 0 is not changed to 30.
```

TITLE: CEL Examples for optionalOldSelf in Kubernetes CRD Transition Rules
DESCRIPTION: These examples illustrate the usage of `optionalOldSelf` in CEL expressions for Kubernetes CRD validation transition rules. They show how to create ratcheted rules, handle removed enum cases, and validate changes in collection sizes, leveraging `oldSelf` for conditional logic.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/tasks/extend-kubernetes/custom-resources/custom-resource-definitions.md#_snippet_57

LANGUAGE: CEL
CODE:
```
self.foo == ""foo"" || (oldSelf.hasValue() && oldSelf.value().foo != ""foo"")
```

LANGUAGE: CEL
CODE:
```
[oldSelf.orValue(""""), self].all(x, [""OldCase1"", ""OldCase2""].exists(case, x == case)) || [""NewCase1"", ""NewCase2""].exists(case, self == case) || [""NewCase""].has(self)
```

LANGUAGE: CEL
CODE:
```
oldSelf.optMap(o, o.size()).orValue(0) < 4 || self.size() >= 4
```

TITLE: Example Kubernetes AdmissionReview Object for Update Request
DESCRIPTION: This JSON example illustrates the detailed structure of an `AdmissionReview` API object for a request to update the `scale` subresource of an `apps/v1` `Deployment`. It includes fields such as `uid`, `kind`, `resource`, `operation`, `userInfo`, `object` (new state), `oldObject` (existing state), and `options` for the operation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/access-authn-authz/extensible-admission-controllers.md#_snippet_11

LANGUAGE: json
CODE:
```
{
  ""apiVersion"": ""admission.k8s.io/v1"",
  ""kind"": ""AdmissionReview"",
  ""request"": {
    ""uid"": ""705ab4f5-6393-11e8-b7cc-42010a800002"",
    ""kind"": {
      ""group"": ""autoscaling"",
      ""version"": ""v1"",
      ""kind"": ""Scale""
    },
    ""resource"": {
      ""group"": ""apps"",
      ""version"": ""v1"",
      ""resource"": ""deployments""
    },
    ""subResource"": ""scale"",
    ""requestKind"": {
      ""group"": ""autoscaling"",
      ""version"": ""v1"",
      ""kind"": ""Scale""
    },
    ""requestResource"": {
      ""group"": ""apps"",
      ""version"": ""v1"",
      ""resource"": ""deployments""
    },
    ""requestSubResource"": ""scale"",
    ""name"": ""my-deployment"",
    ""namespace"": ""my-namespace"",
    ""operation"": ""UPDATE"",
    ""userInfo"": {
      ""username"": ""admin"",
      ""uid"": ""014fbff9a07c"",
      ""groups"": [
        ""system:authenticated"",
        ""my-admin-group""
      ],
      ""extra"": {
        ""some-key"": [
          ""some-value1"",
          ""some-value2""
        ]
      }
    },
    ""object"": {
      ""apiVersion"": ""autoscaling/v1"",
      ""kind"": ""Scale""
    },
    ""oldObject"": {
      ""apiVersion"": ""autoscaling/v1"",
      ""kind"": ""Scale""
    },
    ""options"": {
      ""apiVersion"": ""meta.k8s.io/v1"",
      ""kind"": ""UpdateOptions""
    },
    ""dryRun"": false
  }
}
```

TITLE: Kubernetes Webhook Rule API Versions API Reference

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
webhooks.rules.apiVersions ([]string)
  Description: APIVersions is the API versions the resources belong to. '*' is all versions. If '*' is present, the length of the slice must be one. Required.
```

TITLE: Examples for creating Kubernetes ConfigMaps
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates various ways to create a Kubernetes ConfigMap using `kubectl create configmap`, including from files, directories, literal values, and environment files. Each example illustrates a common use case for populating ConfigMaps with data.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubectl/generated/kubectl_create/kubectl_create_configmap.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
  # Create a new config map named my-config based on folder bar
  kubectl create configmap my-config --from-file=path/to/bar
  
  # Create a new config map named my-config with specified keys instead of file basenames on disk
  kubectl create configmap my-config --from-file=key1=/path/to/bar/file1.txt --from-file=key2=/path/to/bar/file2.txt
  
  # Create a new config map named my-config with key1=config1 and key2=config2
  kubectl create configmap my-config --from-literal=key1=config1 --from-literal=key2=config2
  
  # Create a new config map named my-config from the key=value pairs in the file
  kubectl create configmap my-config --from-file=path/to/bar
  
  # Create a new config map named my-config from an env file
  kubectl create configmap my-config --from-env-file=path/to/foo.env --from-env-file=path/to/bar.env
```

```
PodMetricsList:
  description: PodMetricsList is a list of PodMetrics.
  fields:
    apiVersion:
      type: string
      value: metrics.k8s.io/v1beta1
    kind:
      type: string
      value: PodMetricsList
    metadata:
      type: meta/v1.ListMeta
      required: true
      description: Standard list metadata. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#types-kinds
    items:
      type: []PodMetrics
      required: true
      description: List of pod metrics.
```

TITLE: kubectl exec Command Examples
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates various ways to use `kubectl exec` to run commands, interact with containers, and handle arguments. Examples include getting output from a pod, specifying a container, using interactive terminal mode, listing directory contents, and executing commands on pods identified by deployment or service.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubectl/generated/kubectl_exec/_index.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: Shell
CODE:
```
# Get output from running the 'date' command from pod mypod, using the first container by default
kubectl exec mypod -- date
  
# Get output from running the 'date' command in ruby-container from pod mypod
kubectl exec mypod -c ruby-container -- date
  
# Switch to raw terminal mode; sends stdin to 'bash' in ruby-container from pod mypod
# and sends stdout/stderr from 'bash' back to the client
kubectl exec mypod -c ruby-container -i -t -- bash -il
  
# List contents of /usr from the first container of pod mypod and sort by modification time
# If the command you want to execute in the pod has any flags in common (e.g. -i),
# you must use two dashes (--) to separate your command's flags/arguments
# Also note, do not surround your command and its flags/arguments with quotes
# unless that is how you would execute it normally (i.e., do ls -t /usr, not ""ls -t /usr"")
kubeclt exec mypod -i -t -- ls -t /usr
  
# Get output from running 'date' command from the first pod of the deployment mydeployment, using the first container by default
kubectl exec deploy/mydeployment -- date
  
# Get output from running 'date' command from the first pod of the service myservice, using the first container by default
kubectl exec svc/myservice -- date
```

TITLE: HTTP Authorization Header for Static Bearer Token Authentication
DESCRIPTION: Example of an HTTP Authorization header demonstrating how to include a static bearer token in a request to the Kubernetes API server.

TITLE: Requesting Watch Bookmarks for Resource Version Updates
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to enable and receive `BOOKMARK` events during a watch operation by setting `allowWatchBookmarks=true`. These events provide periodic updates on the current `resourceVersion` without indicating a change to an object, helping clients mitigate the impact of short history windows.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/using-api/api-concepts.md#_snippet_14

LANGUAGE: http
CODE:
```
GET /api/v1/namespaces/test/pods?watch=1&resourceVersion=10245&allowWatchBookmarks=true
---
200 OK
Transfer-Encoding: chunked
Content-Type: application/json

{
  ""type"": ""ADDED"",
  ""object"": {""kind"": ""Pod"", ""apiVersion"": ""v1"", ""metadata"": {""resourceVersion"": ""10596"", ...}, ...}
}
...
{
  ""type"": ""BOOKMARK"",
  ""object"": {""kind"": ""Pod"", ""apiVersion"": ""v1"", ""metadata"": {""resourceVersion"": ""12746""} }
}
```

TITLE: APIServiceStatus
DESCRIPTION: APIServiceStatus contains derived information about an API server
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/cluster-resources/api-service-v1.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
APIServiceStatus:
  conditions ([]APIServiceCondition): Patch strategy: merge on key `type`. Map: unique values on key type will be kept during a merge. Current service state of apiService.
    APIServiceCondition: APIServiceCondition describes the state of an APIService at a particular point
      status (string), required: Status is the status of the condition. Can be True, False, Unknown.
      type (string), required: Type is the type of the condition.
      lastTransitionTime (Time): Last time the condition transitioned from one status to another.
        Time: Time is a wrapper around time.Time which supports correct marshaling to YAML and JSON. Wrappers are provided for many of the factory methods that the time package offers.
      message (string): Human-readable message indicating details about last transition.
      reason (string): Unique, one-word, CamelCase reason for the condition's last transition.
```

TITLE: Kubectl Command-Line Options Reference
DESCRIPTION: Detailed documentation for various command-line flags and arguments available for kubectl commands, including their types, default values, and functional descriptions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubectl/generated/kubectl_apply/_index.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--all
  Select all resources in the namespace of the specified resource types.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--allow-missing-template-keys (Default: true)
  If true, ignore any errors in templates when a field or map key is missing in the template. Only applies to golang and jsonpath output formats.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--cascade string[=""background""] (Default: ""background"")
  Must be ""background"", ""orphan"", or ""foreground"". Selects the deletion cascading strategy for the dependents (e.g. Pods created by a ReplicationController). Defaults to background.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--dry-run string[=""unchanged""] (Default: ""none"")
  Must be ""none"", ""server"", or ""client"". If client strategy, only print the object that would be sent, without sending it. If server strategy, submit server-side request without persisting the resource.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--field-manager string (Default: ""kubectl-client-side-apply"")
  Name of the manager used to track field ownership.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
-f, --filename strings
  The files that contain the configurations to apply.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--force
  If true, immediately remove resources from API and bypass graceful deletion. Note that immediate deletion of some resources may result in inconsistency or data loss and requires confirmation.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--force-conflicts
  If true, server-side apply will force the changes against conflicts.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--grace-period int (Default: -1)
  Period of time in seconds given to the resource to terminate gracefully. Ignored if negative. Set to 1 for immediate shutdown. Can only be set to 0 when --force is true (force deletion).
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
-h, --help
  help for apply
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
-k, --kustomize string
  Process a kustomization directory. This flag can't be used together with -f or -R.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--openapi-patch (Default: true)
  If true, use openapi to calculate diff when the openapi presents and the resource can be found in the openapi spec. Otherwise, fall back to use baked-in types.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
-o, --output string
  Output format. One of: (json, yaml, name, go-template, go-template-file, template, templatefile, jsonpath, jsonpath-as-json, jsonpath-file).
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--overwrite (Default: true)
  Automatically resolve conflicts between the modified and live configuration by using values from the modified configuration
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--prune
  Automatically delete resource objects, that do not appear in the configs and are created by either apply or create --save-config. Should be used with either -l or --all.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
--prune-allowlist strings
  Overwrite the default allowlist with <group/version/kind> for --prune
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
-R, --recursive
  Process the directory used in -f, --filename recursively. Useful when you want to manage related manifests organized within the same directory.
```

TITLE: COSI Kubernetes Object Storage API Definitions
DESCRIPTION: The COSI API defines Kubernetes objects for managing object storage buckets and their access. These APIs provide abstractions similar to PersistentVolume and PersistentVolumeClaim for file/block storage, enabling Kubernetes-native provisioning and access control for object storage resources.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2022-09-02-cosi-kubernetes-object-storage-management.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
COSI API Overview:
  Purpose: Standardize object storage management within Kubernetes.
  Core Abstraction: Buckets.

  Bucket Management APIs:
    Bucket:
      Description: Represents a provisioned object storage bucket. Analogous to Kubernetes PersistentVolume.
      Role: The fundamental unit of abstraction for object storage.
    BucketClass:
      Description: Defines the characteristics and policies for buckets. Analogous to Kubernetes StorageClass.
      Role: Used by administrators to set broad policies and limits for bucket provisioning.
    BucketClaim:
      Description: A request for an object storage bucket by a user/workload. Analogous to Kubernetes PersistentVolumeClaim.
      Role: Allows cluster operators to provision and utilize buckets within administrator-defined limits.

  Bucket Access Management APIs:
    BucketAccess:
      Description: Defines access credentials and policies required to access a specific bucket.
      Role: Manages authentication and authorization for bucket access.
    BucketAccessClass:
      Description: Defines policies for how access credentials are obtained and managed for buckets.
      Role: Used by administrators to restrict who can access which buckets and under what conditions.
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API Endpoint Parameters and Responses
DESCRIPTION: This snippet details the various parameters that can be used when interacting with a Kubernetes API endpoint, including path, query, and body parameters. It also lists the standard HTTP response codes and their meanings for successful and unauthorized requests.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/cluster-resources/lease-candidate-v1beta1.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameters:
- namespace (in path): string, required
  Description: Object's namespace. See common parameters for details.
- body: DeleteOptions
  Description: Options for deleting resources. See common definitions for DeleteOptions.
- continue (in query): string
  Description: The continue token for paginated list requests. See common parameters.
- dryRun (in query): string
  Description: If 'true', modifications will not be persisted. See common parameters.
- fieldSelector (in query): string
  Description: Selector to filter objects by fields. See common parameters.
- gracePeriodSeconds (in query): integer
  Description: The duration in seconds before the object should be deleted. See common parameters.
- ignoreStoreReadErrorWithClusterBreakingPotential (in query): boolean
  Description: If true, ignore errors from store reads that could break the cluster. See common parameters.
- labelSelector (in query): string
  Description: Selector to filter objects by labels. See common parameters.
- limit (in query): integer
  Description: Maximum number of items to return. See common parameters.
- pretty (in query): string
  Description: If 'true', output is pretty printed. See common parameters.
- propagationPolicy (in query): string
  Description: Garbage collection propagation policy. See common parameters.
- resourceVersion (in query): string
  Description: Resource version for consistency. See common parameters.
- resourceVersionMatch (in query): string
  Description: How resourceVersion is applied to list calls. See common parameters.
- sendInitialEvents (in query): boolean
  Description: If 'true', watch starts with current objects. See common parameters.
- timeoutSeconds (in query): integer
  Description: Timeout for list/watch calls. See common parameters.

Response:
- 200 (Status): OK
  Description: Successful operation, returns a Status object. See common definitions for Status.
- 401: Unauthorized
  Description: Request requires authentication.
```

TITLE: List or Watch Cluster-Scoped Ingress Objects
DESCRIPTION: API endpoint and parameters for listing or watching all Kubernetes Ingress resources across all namespaces.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/service-resources/ingress-v1.md#_snippet_8

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
HTTP Request:
  GET /apis/networking.k8s.io/v1/ingresses

Parameters:
  - allowWatchBookmarks (in query): boolean
    Description: Allow watch bookmarks.
  - continue (in query): string
    Description: The continue token for pagination.
  - fieldSelector (in query): string
    Description: A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields.
  - labelSelector (in query): string
    Description: A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their labels.
  - limit (in query): integer
    Description: The maximum number of items to return.
  - pretty (in query): string
    Description: If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.
  - resourceVersion (in query): string
    Description: When specified, restricts the results to objects at that resource version.
  - resourceVersionMatch (in query): string
    Description: Matches objects at the given resource version.
  - sendInitialEvents (in query): boolean
    Description: When specified, sends initial events to the watch stream.
  - timeoutSeconds (in query): integer
    Description: Timeout for the list/watch call.
  - watch (in query): boolean
    Description: Watch for changes to the described resources.

Response:
  - 200 (IngressList): OK
  - 401: Unauthorized
```

TITLE: Create Kustomize Base Directory and Resources
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates the creation of a Kustomize 'base' directory, which serves as a reusable set of Kubernetes resources. It includes defining a `deployment.yaml`, a `service.yaml`, and a `kustomization.yaml` that simply lists these resources, establishing a foundational configuration that can be extended by overlays.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/tasks/manage-kubernetes-objects/kustomization.md#_snippet_32

LANGUAGE: shell
CODE:
```
# Create a directory to hold the base
mkdir base
# Create a base/deployment.yaml
cat <<EOF > base/deployment.yaml
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: my-nginx
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      run: my-nginx
  replicas: 2
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        run: my-nginx
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: my-nginx
        image: nginx
EOF

# Create a base/service.yaml file
cat <<EOF > base/service.yaml
apiVersion: v1
kind: Service
metadata:
  name: my-nginx
  labels:
    run: my-nginx
spec:
  ports:
  - port: 80
    protocol: TCP
  selector:
    run: my-nginx
EOF
# Create a base/kustomization.yaml
cat <<EOF > base/kustomization.yaml
resources:
- deployment.yaml
- service.yaml
EOF
```

TITLE: Kubernetes Validation Rule Scoping: Scalar Example
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates applying a CEL validation rule directly to a scalar field, where `self` refers to the scalar value itself.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/tasks/extend-kubernetes/custom-resources/custom-resource-definitions.md#_snippet_48

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
# ...
openAPIV3Schema:
  type: object
  properties:
    spec:
      type: object
      properties:
        # ...
        foo:
          type: integer
          x-kubernetes-validations:
          - rule: ""self > 0""
```

TITLE: List or Watch Namespaced Kubernetes DaemonSets API
DESCRIPTION: Documents the API parameters and responses for listing or watching DaemonSet objects within a specific Kubernetes namespace. This operation allows filtering, pagination, and watching for changes.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/workload-resources/daemon-set-v1.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
HTTP Request: GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets
Parameters:
  - namespace (in path): string, required
  - allowWatchBookmarks (in query): boolean
  - continue (in query): string
  - fieldSelector (in query): string
  - labelSelector (in query): string
  - limit (in query): integer
  - pretty (in query): string
  - resourceVersion (in query): string
  - resourceVersionMatch (in query): string
  - sendInitialEvents (in query): boolean
  - timeoutSeconds (in query): integer
  - watch (in query): boolean
Response:
  - 200 (DaemonSetList): OK
  - 401: Unauthorized
```

TITLE: Deploy Stateful Workload with Legacy APIs
DESCRIPTION: This YAML defines a `PersistentVolumeClaim` and a `Pod` that uses it, demonstrating how to deploy a stateful workload using legacy Kubernetes APIs. This deployment confirms that CSI migration is functioning correctly by allowing the legacy API to provision storage via the CSI driver.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2019-12-09-csi-volume-migration-beta.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: v1
kind: PersistentVolumeClaim
metadata:
  name: test-disk
spec:
  storageClassName: standard
  accessModes:
    - ReadWriteOnce
  resources:
    requests:
      storage: 10Gi
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
metadata:
  name: web-server
spec:
  containers:
   - name: web-server
     image: nginx
     volumeMounts:
       - mountPath: /var/lib/www/html
         name: mypvc
  volumes:
   - name: mypvc
     persistentVolumeClaim:
       claimName: test-disk
```

TITLE: List or Watch APIService Objects
DESCRIPTION: Lists or watches all APIService objects. This operation supports various filtering and pagination options to retrieve a subset of resources or monitor changes.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubernetes-api/cluster-resources/api-service-v1.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
HTTP Request:
  GET /apis/apiregistration.k8s.io/v1/apiservices

Parameters:
  - allowWatchBookmarks (in query): boolean
    Description: allowWatchBookmarks requests watch events with type ""BOOKMARK"".
  - continue (in query): string
    Description: The continue token for pagination.
  - fieldSelector (in query): string
    Description: A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields.
  - labelSelector (in query): string
    Description: A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their labels.
  - limit (in query): integer
    Description: limit is a maximum number of responses to return for a list call.
  - pretty (in query): string
    Description: If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.
  - resourceVersion (in query): string
    Description: resourceVersion sets a constraint on what resource versions a request may be served from.
  - resourceVersionMatch (in query): string
    Description: resourceVersionMatch determines how resourceVersion is applied to list calls.
  - sendInitialEvents (in query): boolean
    Description: When specified, the system will send an initial list of items and then watch for changes.
  - timeoutSeconds (in query): integer
    Description: Timeout for the list/watch call.
  - watch (in query): boolean
    Description: Watch for changes to the described resources and return events as changes occur.

Response:
  - 200 (APIServiceList): OK
  - 401: Unauthorized
```

TITLE: Define Service with Backend Application Protocol
DESCRIPTION: Gateway API 1.2.0 now supports honoring the `appProtocol` field in Service and EndpointSlice resources, which specifies the L7 protocol a Service supports. This example shows a Kubernetes Service configured to use WebSocket over cleartext (`kubernetes.io/ws`), allowing an HTTPRoute to automatically upgrade connections.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2024-11-21-gateway-api-v1-2/index.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: v1

metadata:
  name: websocket-service
  namespace: my-namespace
spec:
  selector:
    app.kubernetes.io/name: websocket-app
  ports:
    - name: http
      port: 80
      targetPort: 9376
      protocol: TCP
      appProtocol: kubernetes.io/ws
```

TITLE: Enable Session Persistence with BackendLBPolicy in Kubernetes Gateway API
DESCRIPTION: This configuration example shows how to enable cookie-based session persistence for a service using the `BackendLBPolicy`. It defines the session name, absolute and idle timeouts, and configures the cookie to be a session cookie, providing service-level load balancing policy.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2024-05-09-gateway-api-v1.1/index.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: gateway.networking.k8s.io/v1alpha2
kind: BackendLBPolicy
metadata:
  name: lb-policy
  namespace: foo-ns
spec:
  targetRefs:
  - group: core
    kind: service
    name: foo
  sessionPersistence:
    sessionName: foo-session
    absoluteTimeout: 1h
    idleTimeout: 30m
    type: Cookie
    cookieConfig:
      lifetimeType: Session
```

TITLE: Example Kubelet Bootstrap Kubeconfig File
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet illustrates a sample kubeconfig file used for kubelet bootstrapping. LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```

    certificate-authority: /var/lib/kubernetes/ca.pem
    server: https://my.server.example.com:6443
  name: bootstrap
contexts:
- context:
    cluster: bootstrap
    user: kubelet-bootstrap
  name: bootstrap
current-context: bootstrap
preferences: {}
users:
- name: kubelet-bootstrap
  user:
    token: 07401b.f395accd246ae52d

TITLE: Joining Deprecated API Metrics with Request Totals using kubectl and jq
DESCRIPTION: This `kubectl` command, combined with `prom2json` and `jq`, joins information from `apiserver_requested_deprecated_apis` with `apiserver_request_total` metrics. It provides more detailed insights into requests made to deprecated APIs, including the HTTP code, component, content type, verb, and scope of the requests.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2020-09-03-warnings/index.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
kubectl get --raw /metrics | prom2json | jq '
  # set $deprecated to a list of deprecated APIs
  [
    .[] |
    select(.name==""apiserver_requested_deprecated_apis"").metrics[].labels |
    {group,version,resource}
  ] as $deprecated 
  
  |
  
  # select apiserver_request_total metrics which are deprecated
  .[] | select(.name==""apiserver_request_total"").metrics[] |
  select(.labels | {group,version,resource} as $key | $deprecated | index($key))
'
```

TITLE: Kubernetes API Core Functionality and Overview
DESCRIPTION: This section describes the fundamental role of the Kubernetes API as the central interface for managing cluster resources and state. It highlights its RESTful nature, declarative configuration capabilities, and extensibility for custom resources.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/glossary/kubernetes-api.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Kubernetes API:
  Type: Application serving Kubernetes functionality.
  Interface: RESTful.
  Primary Function: Stores the state of the cluster.
  Resource Management:
    - All Kubernetes resources and ""records of intent"" are stored as API objects.
    - Modifications are performed via RESTful calls to the API.
  Configuration Management:
    - Enables declarative configuration.
  User Interaction:
    - Direct interaction with the API is possible.
    - Interaction via tools (e.g., `kubectl`) is common.
  Extensibility:
    - The core Kubernetes API is flexible.
    - Supports extension to include custom resources.
```

TITLE: kubectl create ingress examples
DESCRIPTION: Various examples demonstrating how to use `kubectl create ingress` to configure different Ingress scenarios, including TLS, custom classes, annotations, multiple paths/hosts, and default backends.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/kubectl/generated/kubectl_create/kubectl_create_ingress.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Create a single ingress called 'simple' that directs requests to foo.com/bar to svc
# svc1:8080 with a TLS secret ""my-cert""
kubectl create ingress simple --rule=""foo.com/bar=svc1:8080,tls=my-cert""
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Create a catch all ingress of ""/path"" pointing to service svc:port and Ingress Class as ""otheringress""
kubectl create ingress catch-all --class=otheringress --rule=""/path=svc:port""
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Create an ingress with two annotations: ingress.annotation1 and ingress.annotations2
kubectl create ingress annotated --class=default --rule=""foo.com/bar=svc:port"" \
--annotation ingress.annotation1=foo \
--annotation ingress.annotation2=bla
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Create an ingress with the same host and multiple paths
kubectl create ingress multipath --class=default \
--rule=""foo.com/=svc:port"" \
--rule=""foo.com/admin/=svcadmin:portadmin""
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Create an ingress with multiple hosts and the pathType as Prefix
kubectl create ingress ingress1 --class=default \
--rule=""foo.com/path*=svc:8080"" \
--rule=""bar.com/admin*=svc2:http""
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Create an ingress with TLS enabled using the default ingress certificate and different path types
kubectl create ingress ingtls --class=default \
--rule=""foo.com/=svc:https,tls"" \
--rule=""foo.com/path/subpath*=othersvc:8080""
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Create an ingress with TLS enabled using a specific secret and pathType as Prefix
kubectl create ingress ingsecret --class=default \
--rule=""foo.com/*=svc:8080,tls=secret1""
```

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
# Create an ingress with a default backend
kubectl create ingress ingdefault --class=default \
--default-backend=defaultsvc:http \
--rule=""foo.com/*=svc:8080,tls=secret1""
```

TITLE: Kubernetes Gateway API: Minimal HTTPRoute Resource Definition
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet defines a basic Kubernetes HTTPRoute resource. An HTTPRoute specifies how HTTP requests are routed from a Gateway listener to backend network endpoints. This example routes HTTP traffic from Gateway `example-gateway` with the `Host` header `www.example.com` and path prefix `/login` to the `example-svc` Service on port `8080`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/concepts/services-networking/gateway.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: gateway.networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: HTTPRoute
metadata:
  name: example-httproute
spec:
  parentRefs:
  - name: example-gateway
  hostnames:
  - ""www.example.com""
  rules:
  - matches:
    - path:
        type: PathPrefix
        value: /login
    backendRefs:
    - name: example-svc
      port: 8080
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Configure Gateway Client Certificate Verification with Kubernetes Gateway API
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates how to configure client certificate verification for a Gateway Listener using the new `frontendValidation` field within the `tls` section. It specifies a ConfigMap containing CA Certificates to be used as a trust anchor for validating client certificates.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2024-05-09-gateway-api-v1.1/index.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: gateway.networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: Gateway
metadata:
  name: client-validation-basic
spec:
  gatewayClassName: acme-lb
  listeners:
  - name: foo-https
    protocol: HTTPS
    port: 443
    hostname: foo.example.com
    tls:
      certificateRefs:
      - kind: Secret
        group: """"
        name: foo-example-com-cert
      frontendValidation:
        caCertificateRefs:
        - kind: ConfigMap
          group: """"
          name: foo-example-com-ca-cert
```

NodeMetricsList:
  description: NodeMetricsList is a list of NodeMetrics.
  fields:
    apiVersion:
      type: string
      value: metrics.k8s.io/v1beta1

      type: string
      value: NodeMetricsList

      description: List of node metrics.

TITLE: Kubernetes API: VolumeGroupSnapshot Object Definition
DESCRIPTION: Defines the API object created by users or automation to request the creation of a volume group snapshot for multiple PersistentVolumeClaims. It tracks the snapshot operation's status, including timestamp and readiness.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/blog/_posts/2023-05-08-volume-group-snapshot-alpha.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
VolumeGroupSnapshot:
  Purpose: Request creation of a volume group snapshot for multiple persistent volume claims.
  Properties:
    - timestamp: The timestamp when the volume group snapshot was taken.
    - readyToUse: A boolean indicating whether the volume group snapshot is ready to use.
  Lifecycle:
    - Creation: Represents a desire to create a cluster resource (a group snapshot).
    - Deletion: Represents a desire to delete a cluster resource (a group snapshot).
```

TITLE: Kubernetes Gateway API: Minimal Gateway Resource Definition
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet defines a basic Kubernetes Gateway resource. A Gateway represents an instance of traffic handling infrastructure, such as a load balancer or proxy, configured to listen for HTTP traffic on a specified port. In this example, the Gateway listens on port 80, and its network address will be assigned by the implementation's controller.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/concepts/services-networking/gateway.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
apiVersion: gateway.networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: Gateway
metadata:
  name: example-gateway
spec:
  gatewayClassName: example-class
  listeners:
  - name: http
    protocol: HTTP
    port: 80
```

TITLE: Kubernetes Role Rules for Reading Pods
DESCRIPTION: Defines rules for a Kubernetes Role or ClusterRole to allow 'get', 'list', and 'watch' operations on 'pods' resources within the core API group.
SOURCE: https://github.com/kubernetes/website/blob/main/content/en/docs/reference/access-authn-authz/rbac.md#_snippet_14

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
rules:
- apiGroups: [""""]
  #
  # at the HTTP level, the name of the resource for accessing Pod
  # objects is ""pods""
  resources: [""pods""]
  verbs: [""get"", ""list"", ""watch""]
```","kubernetes",""
